Distribution of Bequest to 'Aqarib' with One Paternal and Two Maternal Uncles
Ruling when bequest to aqarib with one paternal and two maternal uncles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the distribution of a bequest made to 'aqarib' when only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles survive, and explain the principle that the plural form requires at least two recipients.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'aqarib' (plural) requires at least two recipients; a single relative cannot take the whole.

This lesson presents a specific ruling from the Hanafi school on how to distribute a bequest when the testator uses the plural term 'aqarib' (relatives) and only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles survive. The key is the grammatical plural: the word 'aqarib' demands at least two individuals. Understanding this lexical principle prevents the mistake of giving the entire bequest to a single relative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest wording
Recognize that the testator used the plural word 'aqarib' (relatives) in the bequest. In Hanafi legal interpretation, a plural form carries a specific requirement: it must refer to at least two persons.
This is not about the number of categories but the total number of individuals.
2
Count the surviving relatives
List the surviving relatives: one paternal uncle (singular) and two maternal uncles (plural). Note which categories have one individual and which have multiple.
The paternal uncle is a single individual; the maternal uncles are two.
3
Apply the plural principle
Because 'aqarib' requires at least two, the single paternal uncle cannot take the entire bequest. He takes half, and the two maternal uncles together take the other half.
This distribution reflects the lexical necessity, not a preference for maternal over paternal.
4
Confirm the rationale
The ruling analogizes to inheritance law, where plural forms are also interpreted to require at least two. The principle is consistent across Hanafi fiqh.
The bequest is valid and distributed according to the wording.

Source Text

ولو ترک عما و خالین فللعم نصف الوصية والنصف للخالين لانه لا بد من اعتبار معنى الجمع وهو الاثنان في الوصية كما في الميراث
ترجمہ اور اگر موصی نے ایک چا اور ماموں چھوڑے تو چچا کے لئے وصیت کا نصف ہے اور نصف دونوں ماموں کے لئے اس لئے کہ جمع کے معنی کا اعتبار ضروری ہے اور وہ وصیت میں دو ہیں جیسے میراث میں۔ تشریح اگر موصی نے اقرباء کے لئے وصیت کی تھی اور اس نے فقط ایک چا اور دو ماموں چھوڑے ہیں تو چونکہ اقرباء جمع کا صیغہ ہے جس کے لئے کم از کم دو افراد درکار ہیں اور چچا صرف ایک ہے اس لئے وہ چچا صرف نصف کا حقدار ہوگا اور نصف بچ گیا تو اس کو دونوں ماموں میں گئے۔
And if he leaves one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle is half of the bequest, and half for the two maternal uncles, because it is necessary to consider the meaning of plural, which is two, in the bequest as in inheritance. Translation: And if the testator left one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle is half of the bequest, and half for the two maternal uncles, because it is necessary to consider the meaning of plural, and that is two in the bequest as in inheritance. Explanation: If the testator made a bequest for his relatives and he left only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then since 'aqarib' is a plural form requiring at least two individuals, and the paternal uncle is only one, he is entitled to only half, and the remaining half goes to the two maternal uncles.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This ruling addresses a specific scenario where the testator uses the plural term 'aqarib' (relatives) in his bequest, but only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles survive. The principle here is that the plural form necessitates at least two recipients. Since the paternal uncle is a single individual, he cannot take the entire bequest under the plural wording. Therefore, he receives half (as the closest relative if we consider the earlier dispute), and the two maternal uncles together receive the other half. This is consistent with the general rule in inheritance and wills that the plural form requires at least two. Note that this ruling is given without reference to the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn; it seems to follow the view that the meaning of plural must be honored.

Key Terms
جمع (jamm'): Plural; here referring to the grammatical plural in the word 'aqarib'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All to the paternal uncle because he is the closest.
B) All to the maternal uncles because they are two.
C) Half to the paternal uncle and half to the two maternal uncles.
D) The bequest is invalid because there are no two paternal uncles.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to 'aqarib' is divided such that the plural meaning is fulfilled, requiring at least two recipients; a single relative cannot take the whole.

Bequest to 'Aqarib' with a Single Recipient
Ruling on bequest to 'aqarib' when only one paternal uncle survives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a bequest is made to 'aqarib' and only one paternal uncle survives, and apply the principle of plural wording to derive the share.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'aqarib' (plural) requires at least two recipients; one relative takes only half the bequest.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the wording of a bequest matters. Using a plural term like 'aqarib' implies multiple recipients. If only one relative actually exists, that single relative does not receive the entire bequest—only half. This lesson explains the reasoning and the resulting share.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the wording
The testator made a bequest using the plural word 'aqarib' (relatives). Note that the plural form in Arabic implies at least two.
If the testator had used a singular word like 'my paternal uncle', the ruling would differ.
2
Determine the number of recipients
The testator has only one living paternal uncle. Therefore, the bequest intended for multiple relatives cannot be fully assigned to this single uncle.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of plural wording
When a bequest is made to a category using a plural term, the bequest is divided equally among the number implied by the plural (minimum two). If only one exists, he receives only half of the bequest. The other half is not considered part of the bequest.
This is based on the principle that the plural form requires at least two for full effect.
4
Calculate the actual share
The bequest itself is limited to one-third of the estate. The uncle receives half of that one-third, i.e., one-sixth of the total estate.
The remaining half of the bequest (one-sixth of the estate) is not given to the uncle; it remains with the heirs.

Source Text

ـه نصف الثل

ترجمہ اور اگر اس کے لئے ایک بچا ہو تو اس کے لئے ٹکٹ کا نصف ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح اگر موجھی نے جمع کے لفظ سے وصیت کی یعنی لفظ اقرباء کے ساتھ اور موصی کا فقط ایک ہی چچا ہے تو اصول مذکور کے مطابق اس چچا کو صرف ثلث کا نصف ملے گا۔
And if he has one paternal uncle, then for him is half of the third [of the bequest]. Book of Wills. Translation: And if he has one paternal uncle, then for him is half of the third, due to the reason we have explained. Explanation: If the testator made a bequest with the plural form, i.e., the word 'aqarib', and the testator has only one paternal uncle, then according to the mentioned principle, that paternal uncle will only get half of the third.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This ruling clarifies a scenario where the testator uses the plural 'aqarib' for his bequest, but only one paternal uncle survives. Since the plural form requires at least two recipients, the single paternal uncle cannot take the entire bequest. Instead, he receives half of the bequest (which itself is limited to one-third of the estate). The other half is not given to him; presumably it would either be invalid or distributed elsewhere (the text does not specify further, but it implies the bequest is partially effective). The principle is that the plural wording limits the bequest to the number of recipients implied.

Key Terms
ثلث (thulth): One-third; the maximum amount that can be bequeathed in a will.
عم (amm): Paternal uncle.
أقرباء (aqarib): Relatives (plural). In this context, a plural term implying multiple individuals.

B) Half of the bequest.
C) Nothing, because the bequest is invalid.
D) The entire one-third of the estate.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a plural category like 'aqarib' yields only half of the bequest to a single surviving relative.

Priority of Paternal Relatives Over Maternal in Bequests
Ruling on bequest when paternal uncle/aunt and maternal uncle/aunt co-exist

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when paternal and maternal relatives simultaneously exist in a bequest to 'aqarib' and explain why paternal relatives take priority.

Core Idea
Paternal kinship prevails over maternal in bequests to unspecified relatives.

When a Muslim writes a will for his 'aqarib' (relatives) without naming individuals, a priority rule determines who receives the bequest. The Hanafi school holds that paternal relatives are stronger in kinship than maternal ones. This lesson examines the ruling when both paternal and maternal relatives (uncle, aunt) are present, including the surprising point that non-heirs like a paternal aunt can be entitled beneficiaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The text presents a case where the testator leaves four relatives: a paternal uncle, a paternal aunt, a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt. All are alive at the testator's death.
The bequest is made to 'aqarib' (relatives) generally, not to specific individuals.
2
State the ruling
The bequest goes entirely to the paternal uncle and paternal aunt, divided equally between them. The maternal relatives receive nothing.
The ruling is based on the relative strength of kinship (qarabah).
3
Apply the reasoning (ta'lil)
Paternal kinship is 'stronger' (aqwa) than maternal kinship. Therefore, paternal relatives exclude maternal ones when both exist. The equality between paternal uncle and aunt is due to their equal degree of kinship.
The equality is because both are children of the testator's paternal grandparents, thus equally distant.
4
Examine the exception: non-heirs can benefit
Even though the paternal aunt is not a legal heir (she is neither a Quranic sharer nor an asabah), she still receives the bequest. This is analogous to a slave or disbeliever, who also cannot inherit but can be beneficiaries of a will.
The capacity to inherit is not a condition for receiving a bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ترك عما وعمة وخالا وخالة فالوصية للعم والعمة بينهما بالسوية لا ستواء قرابتهما وهى أقوى والعمة وان لم تكن وارثة فهى مستحقة للوصية كما لو كان القريب رقيقاً او كافراً
ترجمہ اور اگر موصی نے ایک چا اور ایک پھوپھی اور ایک ماموں اور ایک خالہ چھوڑے ہوں تو وصیت چا اور پھوپھی کے لئے ہوگی ان دونوں کے درمیان برابر ہو گی ان دونوں کی قرابت کے برابر ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہ قریب چا اور پھوپھی کی ) اقویٰ ہے ( ماموں اور خالہ کی قرابت ہے ) اور پھوپھی اگر چہ وارث نہیں ہے پس وہ وضیت کی مستحق ہے جیسے اگر قرابت غلام یا کافر ہو۔ تشریح چا اور پھوپھی کی قرابت ماموں اور خالہ کی قرابت سے اقویٰ ہے لہذا جب یہ چاروں جمع ہو جائیں تو وصیت چا اور پھوپھی کو ملے گی اور ان دونوں کے درمیان برابر تقسیم کر دی جائے گی کیونکہ دونوں کی قرابت مساوی ہے۔ اور پھوپھی اگر چہ وارث نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ وہ نہ اصحاب الفرائض میں سے ہے اور نہ عصبہ ہے لیکن وصیت کی وہ مستحق ہوگی جیسے کا فراور غلام وارث نہیں ہوتے لیکن اگر اقرباء کے لئے وصیت کی جائے اور اس کے اقرباء میں کا فریا غلام ہے تو وہ وصیت کے حقدار ہوتے ہیں اسی طرح یہاں پھوپھی وصیت کی حقدار ہوگی۔
And if he leaves a paternal uncle, a paternal aunt, a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt, then the bequest is for the paternal uncle and paternal aunt, equally between them, because of the equality of their kinship, and it is stronger. And even if the paternal aunt is not an heir, she is entitled to the bequest, just as if the relative were a slave or an infidel. Translation: And if the testator left a paternal uncle, a paternal aunt, a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt, then the bequest will be for the paternal uncle and paternal aunt, equally between them, due to the equality of their kinship, and this (kinship of paternal uncle and aunt) is stronger (than that of maternal uncle and aunt). And even though the paternal aunt is not an heir, she is entitled to the bequest, just as if the relative were a slave or an infidel. Explanation: The kinship of the paternal uncle and aunt is stronger than that of the maternal uncle and aunt. Therefore, when these four are together, the bequest goes to the paternal uncle and aunt, and it is divided equally between them because their kinship is equal. And even though the paternal aunt is not an heir (she is neither among the Quranic heirs nor an asabah), she is entitled to the bequest, just as a disbeliever or a slave is not an heir but if a bequest is made to relatives and among them there is a disbeliever or a slave, they are entitled to the bequest. Similarly, here the paternal aunt is entitled to the bequest.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This ruling establishes the priority of paternal relatives over maternal relatives in the context of bequests to relatives. When the testator uses the word 'aqarib' or similar plural, and there exist both paternal (uncle, aunt) and maternal (uncle, aunt) relatives, the paternal relatives take the entire bequest to the exclusion of maternal ones. This is because paternal kinship (through the father) is considered stronger than maternal kinship. Furthermore, even if a relative is not an heir (like the paternal aunt, who is neither a Quranic sharer nor an asabah), they are still entitled to receive the bequest. The text draws an analogy to the case of a slave or a disbeliever: they are not heirs, but they can receive a bequest if named. Thus, the capacity to inherit is not a condition for being a beneficiary of a will.

Key Terms
قرابت (qarabah): Kinship; closeness of relation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths to his 'aqarib' and leaves a paternal uncle, paternal aunt, maternal uncle, and maternal aunt, who receives the bequest?
A) All four equally.
B) Only the paternal uncle and maternal uncle.
C) Only the paternal uncle and paternal aunt, equally.
D) Only the maternal relatives because they are weaker.

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to unspecified relatives, paternal relatives (whether heirs or not) take priority over maternal relatives and share equally among themselves.

Will to 'Aqriba with a Single Paternal Uncle
Explains the share of a single relative when will uses plural 'aqriba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the share a single paternal uncle receives when a will is made to 'aqriba and calculate it as half of the bequeathable third.

Core Idea
A will to 'aqriba distributes the third among relatives; one uncle gets half of that third.

When a testator uses the plural term 'aqriba ('relatives') in a will, Hanafi law treats it as a collective bequest. But what if only one relative qualifies? This lesson clarifies that the single relative does not receive the entire bequeathable third but only half of it, based on the principle that the plural form implies at least two recipients.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest type
Recognise that the testator's will uses the plural 'aqriba, indicating a collective distribution among relatives.
Plural form implies more than one.
2
Confirm the sole heir
In this case, only one paternal uncle exists among the relatives.
No other relatives mentioned.
3
Apply the distribution rule
Since the plural requires at least two, the single uncle takes only half of the bequeathable third (one-sixth of the estate).
فله نصف الثلث

Ruling on will using plural 'aqriba and if the testator has one uncle: If he has one paternal uncle, he gets half of the third. The Book of Wills. Translation: And if he has one uncle, he gets half of the third, due to the proof we have mentioned. Explanation: If the testator made a will using the plural word 'aqriba and he has only one paternal uncle, then according to the mentioned principle that uncle receives only half of the third. The closeness of paternal uncle and paternal aunt is stronger than that of maternal uncle and maternal aunt. And if he leaves a paternal uncle, a paternal aunt, a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt, the will is for the paternal uncle and paternal aunt equally between them due to the equality of their closeness, and it is stronger. And the paternal aunt, even if she is not an heir, is entitled to the will, just as if the relative were a slave or disbeliever. Explanation: The closeness of paternal uncle and paternal aunt is stronger than that of maternal uncle and maternal aunt. Therefore when all four are present, the will goes to the paternal uncle and paternal aunt, and it is divided equally between them because their closeness is equal. And the paternal aunt, though not an heir because she is neither among the Quranic heirs nor among the residuaries, is entitled to the will, just as a disbeliever or slave is not an heir but if a will is made for relatives and among his relatives there is a disbeliever or slave, they are entitled to the will. Similarly, here the paternal aunt is entitled to the will.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explains two scenarios regarding a will made using the plural term 'aqriba (relatives). First, if the testator has only one paternal uncle, that uncle receives half of the bequeathable third (i.e., one-sixth of the estate). This is because the plural form implies distribution among all relatives, but if only one exists, he takes the entire share assigned to that category. Second, when both paternal and maternal relatives are present, the paternal uncle and paternal aunt take precedence over maternal uncle and maternal aunt due to their stronger kinship (qarabah). They share the will equally. The text also clarifies that a paternal aunt, though not a legal heir (neither a Quranic sharer nor a residuary), is still entitled to receive the will, just as a slave or disbeliever relative would be.

Key Terms
اقرباء (aqriba): Plural of qarib, meaning relatives. In this context, the term is used in a will to denote a class of beneficiaries.
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate, the maximum bequeathable portion without heir consent.
نصف (nisf): Half, here meaning one-half of the bequeathable third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths one-third to his 'aqriba. He has only one paternal uncle. What does the uncle receive?
A) The entire one-third
B) Half of one-third (one-sixth)
C) One-quarter of one-third
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
When a will uses the plural 'aqriba and only one relative exists, that relative receives half of the bequeathable third.

Will to 'Aqriba: Priority of Paternal Relatives over Maternal
Explains distribution when both paternal and maternal relatives exist

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why paternal relatives (uncle and aunt) take precedence over maternal relatives (uncle and aunt) when a will is made to 'aqriba, and state that a non-heir paternal aunt is entitled to the will.

Core Idea
In a will to 'aqriba, paternal relatives block maternal ones due to stronger qarabah; a non-heir paternal aunt still receives the bequest.

When both paternal and maternal relatives exist, Hanafi law prioritises those with stronger kinship (qarabah). This lesson examines a scenario with a paternal uncle, a paternal aunt, a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt. The paternal pair takes the entire bequest equally, and the paternal aunt qualifies even though she is not a Quranic heir or residuary, analogous to how a slave or disbeliever relative would be entitled.

Guided Path
1
Identify all relatives present
List the four: paternal uncle, paternal aunt, maternal uncle, maternal aunt.
All are relatives under 'aqriba.
2
Apply the rule of qarabah strength
Paternal lineage (عصبة) is stronger than maternal (ذوو الأرحام). Paternal uncle and aunt take precedence over maternal uncle and aunt.
Hanafi: قرابت paternal is أقوى.
3
Distribute equally among paternal relatives
Since paternal uncle and aunt have equal qarabah (both paternal), they share the bequest equally.
No preference based on gender.
4
Confirm the entitlement of the non-heir aunt
Even though the paternal aunt is not a legal heir, she is entitled to the will. This is analogous to a slave or disbeliever relative who also are not heirs but may receive the will.
وصیت entitlement does not require heir status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جمع کے صیغے اقرباء سے وصیت کی اور موصی کا ایک چاہے تو حکم ولو كان له عم واحد فله نصف الثلث كتاب الوصايا ترجمہ اور اگر اس کے لئے ایک بچا ہو تو اس کے لئے ٹکٹ کا نصف ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح اگر موجھی نے جمع کے لفظ سے وصیت کی یعنی لفظ اقرباء کے ساتھ اور موصی کا فقط ایک ہی چچا ہے تو اصول مذکور کے مطابق اس چچا کو صرف ثلث کا نصف ملے گا۔ چا اور پھوپھی کی قرابت ماموں اور خالہ کی قرابت سے اقوی ہے ولو ترك عما وعمة وخالا وخالة فالوصية للعم والعمة بينهما بالسوية لاستواء قرابتهما وهى أقوى والعمة وان لم تكن وارثة فهى مستحقة للوصية كما لو كان القريب رقيقاً او كافراً ترجمہ اور اگر موصی نے ایک چا اور ایک پھوپھی اور ایک ماموں اور ایک خالہ چھوڑے ہوں تو وصیت چا اور پھوپھی کے لئے ہوگی ان دونوں کے درمیان برابر ہو گی ان دونوں کی قرابت کے برابر ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہ قریب چا اور پھوپھی کی ) اقویٰ ہے ( ماموں اور خالہ کی قرابت ہے ) اور پھوپھی اگر چہ وارث نہیں ہے پس وہ وضیت کی مستحق ہے جیسے اگر قرابت غلام یا کافر ہو۔ تشریح چا اور پھوپھی کی قرابت ماموں اور خالہ کی قرابت سے اقویٰ ہے لہذا جب یہ چاروں جمع ہو جائیں تو وصیت چا اور پھوپھی کو ملے گی اور ان دونوں کے درمیان برابر تقسیم کر دی جائے گی کیونکہ دونوں کی قرابت مساوی ہے۔ اور پھوپھی اگر چہ وارث نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ وہ نہ اصحاب الفرائض میں سے ہے اور نہ عصبہ ہے لیکن وصیت کی وہ مستحق ہوگی جیسے کا فراور غلام وارث نہیں ہوتے لیکن اگر اقرباء کے لئے وصیت کی جائے اور اس کے اقرباء میں کا فریا غلام ہے تو وہ وصیت کے حقدار ہوتے ہیں اسی طرح یہاں پھوپھی وصیت کی حقدار ہوگی۔
Ruling on will using plural 'aqriba and if the testator has one uncle: If he has one paternal uncle, he gets half of the third. The Book of Wills. Translation: And if he has one uncle, he gets half of the third, due to the proof we have mentioned. Explanation: If the testator made a will using the plural word 'aqriba and he has only one paternal uncle, then according to the mentioned principle that uncle receives only half of the third. The closeness of paternal uncle and paternal aunt is stronger than that of maternal uncle and maternal aunt. And if he leaves a paternal uncle, a paternal aunt, a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt, the will is for the paternal uncle and paternal aunt equally between them due to the equality of their closeness, and it is stronger. And the paternal aunt, even if she is not an heir, is entitled to the will, just as if the relative were a slave or disbeliever. Explanation: The closeness of paternal uncle and paternal aunt is stronger than that of maternal uncle and maternal aunt. Therefore when all four are present, the will goes to the paternal uncle and paternal aunt, and it is divided equally between them because their closeness is equal. And the paternal aunt, though not an heir because she is neither among the Quranic heirs nor among the residuaries, is entitled to the will, just as a disbeliever or slave is not an heir but if a will is made for relatives and among his relatives there is a disbeliever or slave, they are entitled to the will. Similarly, here the paternal aunt is entitled to the will.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explains two scenarios regarding a will made using the plural term 'aqriba (relatives). First, if the testator has only one paternal uncle, that uncle receives half of the bequeathable third (i.e., one-sixth of the estate). This is because the plural form implies distribution among all relatives, but if only one exists, he takes the entire share assigned to that category. Second, when both paternal and maternal relatives are present, the paternal uncle and paternal aunt take precedence over maternal uncle and maternal aunt due to their stronger kinship (qarabah). They share the will equally. The text also clarifies that a paternal aunt, though not a legal heir (neither a Quranic sharer nor a residuary), is still entitled to receive the will, just as a slave or disbeliever relative would be.

Key Terms
قرابت (qarabah): Kinship closeness, determining priority among relatives for distribution of the will.
عم (amm): Paternal uncle
عمة (ammah): Paternal aunt
خال (khal): Maternal uncle
خالة (khalah): Maternal aunt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All four share equally
B) Only the paternal uncle and aunt share equally
C) Only the paternal uncle receives it all
D) Only the maternal relatives receive it

Key Takeaway
In a will to 'aqriba, paternal relatives exclude maternal ones, and a non-heir paternal aunt is still entitled to the bequest.

Condition of Mahram for Wills to Relatives (Plural Expressions)
States that plural-form wills are void if no mahram relative survives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a will made using a plural expression for relatives and determine whether it is valid or void based on the existence of a mahram relative.

Core Idea
A will to relatives using a plural word is void if no mahram survives, because silah rahmi requires mahram.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the chapter of wills (wasiyyah). The source explains that when a testator uses a collective plural term like 'aqriba or 'relatives', the will is intended for all relatives. However, the validity of such a will depends on a crucial condition: the presence of at least one mahram relative. If no mahram exists, the will becomes void. Let’s explore the reasoning behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a will using a plural expression for relatives (e.g., 'aqriba, dhawi qarabah, ansab). The ruling is that the will is void if no mahram relative survives.
2
Understand the condition (mahram)
The passage states that the will is 'muqayyadah' (conditioned) by the existence of a mahram. Mahram means a relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood or marriage ties.
Mahram includes parents, children, siblings, grandparents, grandchildren, etc.
3
Analyze the underlying reason (silah rahmi)
The purpose of such a will is to maintain family ties (silah rahmi). This purpose is only achievable with mahram relatives. Therefore, if no mahram exists, the purpose fails and the will becomes void.
Sirah rahmi is a key legal consideration (ta'lil) in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply to synonyms
The same ruling applies to any plural expression like 'dhawi qarabatihi', 'li-aqriba'ihi', 'li-ansabihi'. All are considered plural forms and are subject to the same condition.
This is an extension of a previous ruling on the word 'aqriba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جمع کے صیغے اقربا سے وصیت کی اور محرم کوئی نہیں ہے تو وصیت باطل ہے وكذا اذا اوصى لذوى قرابته او لا قربائه او لانسبائه فى جميع ما ذكرنا لان كل ذالك لفظ جمع ولو انعدم المحرم بطلت الوصية لانها مقيدة بهذا الوصف ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی جب کہ موصی نے وصیت کی اپنے قرابت والوں کے لئے یا اپنے اقرباء کے لئے یا اپنے نسب والوں کے لئے ان تمام تفصیلات کے بارے میں جو کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک جمع کا لفظ ہے اور اگر محرم معدوم ہو جائے تو وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ وصیت اس وصف کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔ تشریح جمع کالفظ اقرباء استعمال کرنے کا کیا حکم ہے اس کا جواب ابھی گزر چکا ہے اور یہاں جو الفاظ مذکور ہیں سب جمع کے الفاظ ہیں لہذا ان کا بھی وہی حکم ہو گا جو جمع کے لفظ اقرباء کا گزر چکا ہے اور اگر موصی نے اقرباء کے لئے وصیت کی ہے اور اس کا کوئی حرم نہیں ہے تو وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ اس کی غرض صلہ رحمی ہے اور صلہ رحمی ذور تم محرم کے ساتھ مختص ہے تو محرم کے معدوم ہونے کی صورت میں وصیت ہی کو باطل قرار دیا جائے گا۔
And similarly when he makes a will for his dhawi qarabah (those of his kinship) or for his aqriba (relatives) or for his ansab (kinsmen) in all that we have mentioned, because each of these is a plural word, and if the mahram is non-existent, the will becomes void because it is conditioned by this description. Translation: And similarly when the testator made a will for his relatives or his kinsmen or his familial relations in all the details we have mentioned, because each of them is a plural word; if the mahram is absent, the will becomes void because the will is restricted to this condition. Explanation: The ruling on using the plural word 'aqriba has already passed, and the words mentioned here are all plural words, so their ruling is the same as that of the plural word 'aqriba. And if the testator made a will for 'aqriba and he has no mahram, the will becomes void because its purpose is silah rahmi (maintaining family ties), and silah rahmi is specific to mahram relations. So when the mahram does not exist, the will is declared void.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling on plural words for relatives. The text states that if a testator uses any plural expression such as 'li-dhawi qarabatihi', 'li-aqriba'ihi', or 'li-ansabihi', the same rule applies: the will is intended for all relatives collectively. However, if there is no mahram (a relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as a close blood relative) among the surviving relatives, the will becomes void. The reason is that the purpose of the will is to maintain family ties (silah rahmi), and that is only possible with mahram relatives. The commentary clarifies that the earlier ruling on 'aqriba applies equally to these synonyms.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood or marriage ties; here, a necessary condition for validity of the will.
ذوى قرابته (dhawi qarabatihi): Those who are his relatives; a plural expression equivalent to 'aqriba.
صلہ رحمی (silah rahmi): Maintaining family ties; the underlying purpose of the will to relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A will to relatives using a plural expression is void if no mahram relative survives; the existence of at least one mahram is a necessary condition for validity.

Dispute: Meaning of 'Ahl' in a Will
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interpreting 'ahl' in a will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over the meaning of 'ahl' in a will and identify the evidence used by each side.

Core Idea
When a will is made for 'ahl fulan', Abu Hanifa gives it to the wife only; the Sahibayn include all dependents — a dispute rooted in literal vs. customary meaning.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. When someone makes a will for 'the ahl of so-and-so,' who is entitled? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, disagree on the scope of the word 'ahl.' The difference turns on whether the literal meaning (wife) or the customary meaning (all dependents) should prevail when the word is used absolutely. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi approach to linguistic interpretation and the role of custom (urf) in determining legal meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The issue is the interpretation of the word 'ahl' in a will: when someone bequeaths to 'ahl fulan' (the family/household of so-and-so), who are the intended beneficiaries?
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school, not between madhhabs.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that 'ahl' literally means wife. He cites the Quranic verse 'wa sāra bi-ahlihi' (He set out with his family, interpreted as 'with his wife') and the Arabic verb 'ta'ahhala' meaning 'to marry.' Since no contextual clue (qarīna) is present, the word must be taken in its literal sense.
The principle 'al-mutlaq yunsaraf ila al-haqiqah' governs.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad hold that 'ahl' includes all dependents maintained by the person, such as wife, children, and servants. They rely on custom ('urf) and the Quranic verse 'wa'tūnī bi-ahlikum ajma'īn' (Bring me your families all together), where 'ahl' clearly includes the entire household.
They argue that custom provides a qarīna that shifts the meaning from the literal to the customary.
4
Evaluate the thamarah and tarjih
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Abu Hanifa, only the wife receives the bequest; under the Sahibayn, all dependents share proportionally. In fatwa, the Sahibayn's view is often preferred due to widespread custom, though the text does not explicitly give tarjih.
Later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Hidayah) often adopt the Sahibayn's view as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلاں کے اہل کیلئے وصیت کی تو کون مصداق ہوگا ، اقوال فقہا قال و من اوصى لاهل فلان فهى على زوجته عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يتناول من يعولهم و تضمهم نفقته اعتبارا للعرف وهو مؤيد بالنص قال الله تعالى و اتونی باهلكم اجمعين وله ان اسم الاهل حقيقة في الزوجة يشهد بذالک قوله تعالی و سار باهله ومنه قولهم تاهل ببلدة كذا و المطلق ينصرف الى الحقيقة ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا اور جس نے فلاں کے اہل کے لئے وصیت کی تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وصیت اس کی زوجہ پر محمول ہوگی اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ ان لوگوں کو شامل ہو گی جو اسکی عیال میں ہیں اور جن کو اس کا نفقہ ملتا ہے عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور نص سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے " و أتونی با هلکم اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اہل زوج کے اندر حقیقت ہے فرمان باری تعالی و سار باھلہ اس کا شاہد ہے اور اس سے ان کا قول ہے "تأهل ببلدة كذا " اور مطلق کامل کی جانب منصرف ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح زید نے وصیت کی کہ فلاں کے اہل کو میرا اتنا مال دید یا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اہل سے مراد ز وجہ ہوگی اور وہی وصیت کی حقدار ہوگی ، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اہل میں وہ تمام لوگ داخل ہیں جو زید کی عیال میں داخل ہوں اور زیدان کے نفقہ کا ذمہ دار ہو جیسے بیوی بچے اور غلام و خادم وغیرہ ۔ صاحبین نے عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے یہ بات کہی ہے کہ عرف میں یہ تمام لوگ اہل میں داخل ہوتے ہیں اور اللہ تعالیٰ نے حضرت یوسف کا یہ قول نقل کیا ہے و آتونی با هلكم اجمعین جو انھوں نے اپنے بھائیوں سے کہا تھا کہ تم اپنے اہل وعیال کو میرے پاس لے آؤ تو یہاں اہل میں سب داخل ہیں یعنی بیوی اور بچے اور غلام و خادم وغیرہ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اہل کے حقیقی معنی زوجہ کے ہیں اور دوسروں پر بطریق مجاز بولا جاتا ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے حضرت موسی کے بارے میں ارشاد فرمایا ہے و سار باهله ، یعنی وہ اپنی بیوی کو لے چلے ، اور اہل عرب کا قول ہے "تأهل ببلده كذا ، یعنی فلاں شہر میں اہل بنایا یعنی زوجہ نکاح میں لی۔ اور جب لفظ مطلق بولا جاتا ہے اور کوئی ایسا قرینہ نہ ہو جو اس کو معنی مجازی کی طرف پھیرے دے تو لفظ سے اس کے حقیقی معنی مراد ہوا کرتے ہیں اور اگر کوئی قرینہ موجود ہو جیسے حضرت یوسف کے کلام میں تو معنی مجازی مراد لیے جاتے ہیں۔
One who makes a will for 'ahl' of so-and-so: statements of the jurists. He (the author) said: And whoever makes a will for the 'ahl' of so-and-so, it is upon his wife according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It includes those whom he maintains and whose expenses he bears, considering custom, and this is supported by the text: Allah said, 'And bring me your families all together.' And for Abu Hanifa, the word 'ahl' is literal for wife; witness to that is the saying of Allah, 'And he set out with his family,' and from that is their saying, 'He married in such a town.' And the absolute word is turned to the literal meaning. Translation: The author said: And whoever makes a will for the 'ahl' of so-and-so, then according to Abu Hanifa the will is taken to refer to his wife. And the two (Sahibayn) said: It includes those who are his dependents and for whom he provides maintenance, considering custom, and this is supported by the text: Allah Almighty said, 'And bring me your families all together.' And Abu Hanifa's proof is that the word 'ahl' is literal for wife; the saying of Allah, 'And he set out with his family,' testifies to that, and from this is their saying, 'He married in such a town.' And the absolute word is turned to the literal meaning. Explanation: Zaid made a will stating, 'Give so much of my wealth to the ahl of so-and-so.' According to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'ahl' refers to the wife, and she is entitled to the will. According to the Sahibayn, 'ahl' includes all those who are his dependents and for whom he is responsible for maintenance, such as wife, children, slaves, servants, etc. The Sahibayn considered custom that in common usage all these are included in 'ahl', and they are supported by the text of the Quran: the words of Prophet Yusuf (Joseph), 'Bring me your families all together,' where 'ahl' includes all dependents. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the literal meaning of 'ahl' is wife, and it is used for others metaphorically. Allah said regarding Prophet Musa (Moses), 'And he set out with his family,' meaning his wife. And the Arabs say, 'He took a wife in such a town,' using 'tā'ahhala' for marriage. When the word is used absolutely without a context that indicates the metaphorical meaning, it is taken in its literal sense. If there is a context (like in Yusuf's speech), the metaphorical meaning is intended.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of 'ahl' (household/family) in a will. When someone makes a will for 'the ahl of so-and-so,' who is entitled? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that 'ahl' literally means the wife (zawja), so only the wife receives the will. This is based on linguistic evidence: the Quranic verse about Prophet Musa 'wa sāra bi-ahlihi' (He set out with his family) is interpreted to mean his wife, and the Arabic verb 'ta'ahhala' means to marry. Since the word is used absolutely, it should be taken in its literal sense. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that 'ahl' includes all dependents whom the person maintains, such as wife, children, slaves, and servants. They base this on custom ('urf) and the Quranic verse from Prophet Yusuf: 'wa'tūnī bi-ahlikum ajma'īn' (Bring me your families all together), where 'ahl' clearly includes the entire household. The commentary explains that the difference turns on whether a contextual clue (qarīna) shifts the meaning from literal to metaphorical. Abu Hanifa says no such clue exists in the absolute expression, so the literal meaning (wife) prevails. The Sahibayn argue that custom provides such a clue. This dispute is purely within the Hanafi school; all three are Hanafi imams.

Key Terms
اہل (ahl): Household or family; disputed: Abu Hanifa: wife only; Sahibayn: all dependents.
حقیقت (haqiqah): Literal meaning of a word; Abu Hanifa argues 'ahl' in its literal sense means wife.
عرف (urf): Custom or common usage; Sahibayn use custom to establish the broader meaning of 'ahl'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what does 'ahl' mean when used absolutely in a will?
A) All family members including children and servants
B) Only the wife
C) Only the parents
D) All blood relatives

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of 'ahl' in a will depends on whether one prioritizes literal meaning (Abu Hanifa: wife only) or customary usage (Sahibayn: all dependents), a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Interpreting 'al fulan' in a Will
Defines 'al fulan' as the household

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a will for 'al fulan' is for the ahl al-bayt (household) and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
In a will, 'al fulan' refers to the household, not the tribe.

When a testator uses the word 'al' before a name, it literally means the tribe. However, Hanafi fiqh interprets it narrowly in wills to mean the household. This lesson examines that ruling and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the text
Read the Arabic: 'ولو اوصى لأل فلان فهو لاهل بيته' and its translation.
Focus on the equivalence of 'al' with 'ahl al-bayt'.
2
Identify the literal meaning
Note that 'al' literally means tribe or clan, but the text immediately restricts it.
The text says 'لان الال القبيلة' (because al is the tribe).
3
Understand the legal interpretation
In the context of a will, the word 'al' is interpreted as the ahl al-bayt (household).
The ruling is: 'فهو لاهل بيته'.
4
Apply the ruling
If a testator says 'I give to the al of Zaid', the beneficiaries are Zaid's household, not his entire tribe.
This avoids vagueness and potential invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لفظ 'آل فلاں' سے وصیت کا حکم ولو اوصى لأل فلان فهو لاهل بيته لان الال القبيلة التي ينسب اليها ولو اوصى لاهل بيت فلان يدخل فيه ابوه وجده لان الاب اصل البيت ترجمہ ۔ اور اگر اس نے ال فلاں کے لئے وصیت کی تو یہ وصیت اس کے اہل بیت کے لئے ہوگی اس لئے کہ ال وہ قبیلہ ہے جس کی تشریح: یہاں 'آل' اور 'اہل بیت' کے الفاظ کے احکام بیان کئے جا رہے ہیں۔ اگر کسی نے 'آل فلاں' کے لئے وصیت کی تو اس کا مصداق 'اہل بیت' (گھر والے) ہوں گے، کیونکہ 'آل' قبیلے کو کہتے ہیں جس کی طرف وہ منسوب ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر 'اہل بیت فلاں' کے لئے وصیت کی تو اس میں اس کا باپ اور دادا داخل ہوں گے، کیونکہ باپ گھر کی بنیاد ہے (یعنی گھر کی اصل ہے)۔
Ruling on will for 'al fulan': And if he makes a will for 'al' of so-and-so, it is for his ahl al-bayt, because 'al' is the tribe to which one is attributed. And if he makes a will for 'ahl bayt' of so-and-so, his father and grandfather enter into it, because the father is the origin of the house. Translation: And if he makes a will for 'al fulan', then this will is for his ahl al-bayt (household), because 'al' is the tribe to which one is attributed. And if he makes a will for 'ahl bayt fulan', then his father and grandfather are included in it, because the father is the foundation of the house.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This brief passage provides two definitions. First, when a testator uses the word 'al' (آل) for a person (e.g., 'āl fulān'), the intended beneficiaries are that person's 'ahl al-bayt' (household). The word 'al' refers to the tribe or clan to which someone belongs, but in the context of a will, it is interpreted narrowly as the household. Second, when the phrase 'ahl al-bayt' is used explicitly in a will (e.g., 'ahl bayt fulān'), it includes the father (ab) and grandfather (jadd) because the father is considered the 'origin' or 'foundation' (asl) of the household. This ruling clarifies the scope of these family-related terms in testamentary dispositions.

Key Terms
آل (al): Tribe or lineage; in a will, it refers to the ahl al-bayt (household) of the named person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a will is made for 'al fulan', the beneficiaries are:
A) The tribe
B) The household (ahl al-bayt)
C) The father only
D) The whole village

Key Takeaway
The word 'al' in a will is interpreted as the household (ahl al-bayt), not the tribe.

Interpreting 'ahl bayt fulan' in a Will
Defines 'ahl bayt fulan' as including father and grandfather

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who is included in 'ahl bayt fulan' according to Hanafi fiqh, and explain why the father and grandfather are specifically mentioned.

Core Idea
In a will, 'ahl bayt fulan' includes the father and grandfather because the father is the origin of the house.

The phrase 'ahl al-bayt' appears in many contexts, but in Hanafi wills, it has a specific inclusion. This lesson explores the scope of 'ahl bayt fulan' as defined by the classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the text
Read the Arabic: 'ولو اوصى لاهل بيت فلان يدخل فيه ابوه وجده لان الاب اصل البيت' and its translation.
Focus on the explicit inclusion of father and grandfather.
2
Note the inclusion
The text states that when a will is made for 'ahl bayt fulan', the father and grandfather are included.
The phrase 'يدخل فيه ابوه وجده' clearly specifies these two relatives.
3
Understand the reasoning
The reason given is 'لان الاب اصل البيت' (because the father is the foundation/origin of the house).
This implies the grandfather is included by extension as the root of the father.
4
Apply the ruling
If a testator says 'I give to the ahl bayt of Fatima', the beneficiaries include Fatima's father and grandfather.
Other family members like mother and children are not explicitly mentioned; the ruling only explicitly includes father and grandfather.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
Bequest to Uncountable Individuals is Void
States ruling and reasoning for invalid bequest to countless young men or women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest to an uncountable group and explain the two reasons for its invalidity.

Core Idea
A bequest to countless recipients is void due to severe ignorance and impossibility of execution.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a testator makes a bequest to all the young men or young women of a tribe, and they are so numerous that they cannot be counted. The ruling is that such a bequest is batil (void). The reasoning examines two possible ways to execute the bequest—either giving to all recipients or restricting to the poor among them—and finds both impossible. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the importance of specificity in Islamic inheritance law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that a bequest to countless young men or women of a tribe is void (batil).
2
Examine the first option
Consider making all the countless individuals owners of the bequest. This is impossible because they are uncountable (muta'addir) and there is severe ignorance (jahaalat shadidah) about who they are.
Severe ignorance invalidates the bequest.
3
Examine the second option
Consider directing the bequest only to the poor among them. This is also impossible because the words 'shabban' (young men) and 'ayaamili' (young women) do not imply need or poverty, unlike words such as 'ayatama' (orphans) or 'masakeen' (needy).
Words must indicate need to allow redirection to the poor.
4
Conclude the ruling
Since neither option is possible, the bequest is necessarily void. The Hanafi school holds this position firmly.
The judgement is based on practical impossibility and textual analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ اس نے بنو فلاں کے جوانوں کے لئے وصیت کی ہو اور وہ گنے نہیں جا سکتے یا بہنوفلاں کی جوان عورتوں کے لئے اور وہ گنی نہیں جاسکتیں اس حیثیت سے کہ وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ اس لفظ میں کوئی ایسی چیز نہیں ہے جو حاجت کی خبر دے تو اس کو فقراء کی جانب صرف کرنا ممکن نہ ہوگا اور نہ تمام کو مالک بنا کر اس وصیت کی تصحیح ممکن ہے شدید جہالت کی وجہ سے اور ان تمام کی جانب صرف کے متعد ر ہونے کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح زید نے بنو خالد کے نو جوانوں کے لئے یا بنو خالد کی نوجوان لڑکیوں کے لئے وصیت کی اور یہ نوجوان طبقہ اتنا وسیع ہے کہ جس کو گنا نہیں جا سکتا تو یہاں وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ اگر تمام نو جوانوں کے لئے وصیت کو رکھا جائے اور تمام کو مالک بنایا جائے تو یہ متعد ر ہے چونکہ وہ ان گنت ہیں اور ان میں بے شمار ہونے کی وجہ سے شدید جہالت ہے تو یہ صورت تو ممکن نہیں ہے اور اگر ان میں سے فقط فقراء کے حق میں وصیت کبھی جائے تو یہ بھی ممکن نہیں اس لئے کہ لفظ شبان سے اور اسی طرح لفظ ایا ملی سے کچھ حاجت کے معنی مترشح نہیں ہوئے جیسے ایتام و میان سے حاجت کے معنی مترشح ہوئے تھے لہذا جب کوئی صورت باقی نہ رہے تو ہم نے مجبوراً کہا کہ وصیت باطل ہے۔
Translation: Contrary to the case when he made a bequest to the young men of Banu so-and-so and they cannot be counted, or to the young women of Banu so-and-so and they cannot be counted, in the sense that the bequest will become void because there is nothing in this word that indicates need, so directing it to the poor is not possible, and it is not possible to correct this bequest by making all of them owners due to severe ignorance and due to the difficulty of directing to all of them.
Explanation: Zaid made a bequest to the young men of Banu Khalid or to the young women of Banu Khalid, and this class of youth is so vast that they cannot be counted. So here the bequest will become void because if the bequest is kept for all the youth and all are made owners, it is difficult since they are countless, and due to their being innumerable there is severe ignorance, so this option is not possible. And if the bequest is directed only to the poor among them, this is also not possible because the word 'shabban' (young men) and similarly the word 'ayaamili' (young women) do not convey the meaning of need, unlike the words 'ayama' (orphans) and 'masakeen' (needy) which conveyed the meaning of need. Therefore, when no option remains, we are compelled to say that the bequest is void.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about bequests made to an uncountable group, such as all the young men or young women of a tribe. The ruling: such a bequest is batil (void). The reasoning is twofold: first, there is severe ignorance (jahaalat) because the recipients cannot be identified or counted, making the bequest invalid due to uncertainty. Second, the words used (shabban/youth or ayaamili/young women) do not imply need or poverty, unlike terms like yatama (orphans) or masakeen (needy), which allow direction to those in need. Thus, neither making all of them owners nor restricting it to the poor is possible. The commentator (sharh) confirms that the text of the Hidayah rules this bequest as void. Note: The ruling is based on the principle that a bequest must be to identifiable individuals or a determinate class; if the class is uncountable and without any qualifying description, the bequest fails.

Key Terms
جہالت (jahaalat): Ignorance of the identity or number of recipients to the extent that the bequest cannot be executed.
متعد ر (muta'addir): Difficult or impossible to execute due to the large number of recipients.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because young men are not deserving of charity.
B) Because the number of young men is known but the bequest is too large.
C) Because the recipients are uncountable and no indication of need exists, causing severe ignorance.
D) Because the testator must name each individual.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to countless recipients with no need indicator is void in the Hanafi school because it is impossible to execute and involves severe ignorance.

Minimum Recipients for Bequest to the Poor
Ruling statement with expansion on plural minimum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of recipients required in a bequest to a class (such as fuqara or masakeen) and explain the Hanafi basis for treating plural as two in bequests.

Core Idea
In Hanafi bequests, a plural noun requires at least two recipients — not three as in general Arabic.

This passage addresses a common question: if someone bequeaths to 'the poor' or 'the needy,' how many individuals must receive the bequest? The Hanafi school has a specific rule for bequests: the minimum of a plural noun is two, contrary to the general Arabic rule of three. Understanding this principle ensures that bequests are executed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a bequest (wasiyyah) to a group defined by a singular label (fuqara/masakeen). The ruling is that it is wajib to spend the bequeathed amount on at least two recipients from that group.
The text explicitly says 'wajib' and uses 'ithnayn' (two).
2
Recognize the key principle
The underlying principle is that in the context of bequests (wasiyyah), the plural form (jama') is interpreted to mean a minimum of two, not three. This is a special rule for bequests, distinct from general Arabic usage.
The commentary reminds that this was established earlier in the work (ma marr).
3
Apply the principle to the scenario
If Zaid bequeaths one-third to 'al-fuqara wa al-masakeen', the executor must distribute to at least two poor persons and two needy persons. Giving to only one from either category would violate the wajib requirement.
The text mentions 'ithnayn minhum' – two of them – which the tashreeh clarifies as two poor and two needy.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
This Hanafi rule differs from other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) where plural is generally understood as three. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that a bequest to a class may require a different minimum number of recipients depending on the school followed.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; both positions have their proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقراء اور مساکین کیلئے وصیت کرنا
و فى الوصية للفقراء والمساكين يجب الصرف اثنين منهم اعتباراً لمعنى الجمع واقله اثنان في الوصايا على مامر
ترجمہ اور فقراء اور مساکین کے لئے وصیت کرنے میں ان میں سے دو کی جانب صرف کرنا واجب ہے جمع کے معنی کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور جمع کا اقل فرد وصایا میں دو ہیں اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو گذر چکی ہے۔
تشریح ماقبل میں متعدد مرتبہ یہ بحث گذر چکی ہے کہ وصیت میں جمع کا اقل فرد دو ہے لہذا جب زید نے فقراء اور مساکین کے لئے وصیت کی تو ثلث کو کم از کم دو مسکین اور دو فقیر کو دینا واجب ہوگا۔
Making a bequest for the poor and needy.
'And in the bequest for the poor and needy, it is obligatory to spend to two of them, considering the meaning of plural, and the minimum of plural in bequests is two as per what has passed.'
Translation: And in making a bequest for the poor and needy, it is wajib to direct the bequest to two of them, considering the meaning of plural, and the minimum of plural in bequests is two, according to the detail that has passed.
Explanation: It has been discussed multiple times in the preceding that the minimum of plural in bequests is two. Therefore, when Zaid made a bequest for the poor and needy, it is wajib to give the third (the bequeathed portion) to at least two needy persons and two poor persons.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding bequests made to the poor (fuqara) and needy (masakeen). The ruling: it is wajib (obligatory) to distribute the bequeathed amount to at least two individuals from each category (or at least two total? The text says 'ithnayn minhum' meaning two of them, and the tashreeh explains two poor and two needy. The Hanafi rule is that the minimum of a plural noun (jama') in bequests is two, not three as in general Arabic usage. This is a special ruling for bequests. Therefore, if someone bequeaths one-third of their estate to the poor, it cannot be given to only one poor person; it must go to at least two. Similarly for the needy. The commentary reminds that this principle was established earlier in the work.

Key Terms
فقیر (faqir): A poor person; in this context, a recipient of bequest who is in need.
مسکین (miskin): A needy person; similar to faqir but in some contexts poorer. Used here as a category of recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) At least two poor and two needy persons.
C) At least three poor or needy persons collectively.
D) Only one person from either category.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a class (e.g., 'the poor') in Hanafi fiqh must be distributed to at least two individuals, as the minimum of plural in wasiyyah is two.

Interpretation of 'Banu Fulaan' in Bequests
Intra-Hanafi dispute on linguistic interpretation of 'banun' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when women are included in a bequest to 'Banu Fulaan' according to the mufta bihi Hanafi opinion and evaluate the linguistic proofs of the Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa's later position.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'Banu Fulaan' includes women only if it is a tribal name; otherwise literal 'banun' means males only.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a testator says 'my bequest is to Banu so-and-so', the inclusion of women depends entirely on whether 'Banu Fulaan' is a tribal name or a literal reference to sons. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa (final view) and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), showing how linguistic principles like literal vs figurative meaning decide the ruling. You will learn to identify the two scenarios and apply the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Context
First, determine whether 'Banu Fulaan' is a known tribal name (like Banu Hashim) or a literal reference to the sons of a named individual. This classification triggers different rulings.
If it is a tribal name, the intention is mere attribution (intisab), not specific male offspring.
2
Recall the Hanafi Positions
For the literal scenario, recall the disagreement: Sahibayn and early Abu Hanifa include women; final Abu Hanifa excludes women. Note that the mufta bihi is the final view.
The Sahibayn argue that masculine plural (jama' mudhakkar) generally includes women, as in 'Muslimun'.
3
Apply the Linguistic Rule
Apply the Hanafi uṣūl rule that speech is interpreted literally (ḥaqīqah) unless a qarīnah (contextual indicator) shifts it to figurative (majāz). The word 'banun' literally means male children, so women are not included without a qarīnah.
In the tribal name case, the qarīnah is that it is a proper name for the group, so the literal meaning is overridden.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Imam Abu Hanifa's final view: when 'Banu Fulaan' is not a tribal name, only males are entitled to the bequest.
This tarjīḥ is based on the strength of the literal meaning principle.
5
Include Affiliates if Applicable
If it is a tribal name, remember that affiliates like mawla al-itaqah (freed slaves), mawla al-muwalat (clients by alliance), and hulafaa' (allies) are also included, as they share the same attribution.
This is because the testator intended the group by lineage, not specific individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بنو فلاں کے الفاظ سے کون کون مستحق وصیت قرار پائے گا، اقوال فقہاء
و لو أوصى لبنى فلان يدخل فيه الاناث فى قول أبي حنيفة اول قوله وهو قولهما لان جمع الذكور يتناول الاناث ثم رجع وقال يتناول الذكور خاصة لان حقيقة الاسم للذكور وانتظامه للاناث تجوز الكلام لحقيقته بخلاف ما اذا كان بنو فلان اسم قبيلة او فخذ حيث يتناول الذكور والاناث لأنه ليس يرادبها اعيانها اذ هو نجرد الانتساب كبني ادم ولهذا يدخل فيه مولى العتاقة والموالات و حلفاؤهم
ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے بنو فلاں کے لئے وصیت کی تو ابو حنیفہ کے پہلے قول کے مطابق اور یہی صاحبین کا قول ہے اس میں عورتیں داخل ہوں گی اس لئے کہ جمع مذکر عورتوں کو شامل ہوتی ہے پھر ابوحنیفہ نے اس سے رجوع کر لیا اور فرمایا کہ فقط مردوں کو شامل ہوگا اس لئے کہ لفظ کی حقیقت مردوں کے لئے ہے اور اس کا عورتوں کو شامل ہونا بطور مجاز کے ہے اور کلام اپنی حقیقت پر محمول ہوتا ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ بنو فلاں قبیلہ یافخذ کا نام ہو اس حیثیت سے کہ یہ ( بنو فلاں ) مردوں اور عورتوں کو شامل ہوگا اس لئے کہ اس سے مراد ان کے اعیان نہیں ہوئے اس لئے کہ یہ تو محض انتساب ہے جیسے بنو آدم اور اسی وجہ سے اس میں مولی العتاقہ اور مولی الموالات اور ان کے حلفاء داخل ہیں ۔
تشریح اگر زید نے بنو خالد کے لئے وصیت کی تو اب سوال یہ ہے کہ اس میں لڑکوں کے ساتھ لڑکیاں بھی داخل ہیں یا نہیں تو اس میں تفصیل ہے موسی نے جو بنو خالد کہا ہے تو یہ دیکھا جائے کہ اس نام سے کوئی قبیلہ ہے یا موصی نے محض خالد کے بیٹوں کی تخصیص کے لئے بنون کہا ہے تو اگر اس نام سے کوئی قبیلہ ہو یعنی بن خالد قبیلہ کا نام ہو جیسے بنو ہاشم، بنوامیہ وغیرہ تو اب موصی کا مقصد بعینہ بیٹوں کو مراد لینا نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں بیٹوں کی تخصیص محض انتساب کی غرض سے ہے نہ کہ اس غرض سے کہ خصوصا بنون ہی مراد ہیں جیسے بنو آدم بولا جاتا ہے اور محض انتساب کے لئے ہے جس میں مرد اور عورتیں سب داخل ہیں۔
بہر حال اگر بنو خالد قبیلہ کا نام ہو تو اس میں مرد و عورت سب داخل ہوں گے اور بنو خالد میں بنو خالد کے معتق اور مولی الموالات اور ان کے خلفاء بھی داخل ہوں گے۔ اور اگر بن خالد کی قبیلہ کا نام نہ ہو تو صاحبین کا قول یہ ہے کہ اس میں عورتیں بھی داخل ہوں گی اور یہی امام ابوحنیفہ کا پہلا قول ہے۔
اور امام ابوحنیفہ کا قول مرجوع الیہ یہ ہے کہ اس میں عورتیں داخل نہ ہوں بلکہ یہ صرف مردوں کے لئے ہوگی۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمع مذکر میں بھی عورتیں داخل ہیں جیسے مسلمون میں عورتیں بھی داخل ہیں۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بنون کے حقیقی معنی مردوں کے ہیں اور اس لفظ کا عورتوں کو شامل ہونا مجازا ہے اور جب تک حقیقت سے کوئی قرینہ صارفہ موجود نہ ہو تو کلام کو اس کے حقیقی معنی پر محمول کیا جاتا ہے۔
تنبیہ - مولی العتاقہ ، مثلاً بنوعباس یا بنوامیہ ایک غیر محصور جماعت ہے تو انہوں نے جس غلام کو آزاد کیا وہ ابھی بنو العباس یا بنوامیہ ہی سے کہلائے گا۔ یعنی اسی قبیلہ کی طرف منسوب رہے گا حالانکہ وہ اولاد میں سے نہیں ہے۔ مولی الموالات ، اس کی ایک تفسیر تو وہ ہے جو ہم درس سراجی میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اور دوسری تفسیر یہ ہے کہ جوشخص کسی قبیلہ کے ہاتھ پر مسلمان ہوا تو وہ انھیں میں سے شمار کیا جائے گا اور اس کو مولی الموالات کہا جائے گا۔
حلیف، اس کی جمع حلفاء، جو قسم سے باہم مددگاری پر جمع ہو جائیں۔
تنبیہ - ۲ عرب کے انساب میں بیان اس طرح معروف تھا،
1 اول شعب جس میں کئی قبائل ہوں جیسے قریش کہ شعب تو خزیمہ ہے جس کے تحت میں کئی قبائل ہیں اور شعیب کے تحت میں،
- عمارہ ہے جیسے قریش عمارہ ہے، اور عمارہ کے تحت میں،
بطون ہوتے ہیں چنا نچہ قصی بطن ہے اور وطن کے تحت میں، -۴ فیہ ہوتے ہیں چنا نچہ ہاشم فخذ ہے اور فخذ کے تحت نہیں،
-
فصیل ہے چنا نچہ عباس فصیل ہے۔
Who will be entitled to the bequest from the words 'Banu Fulaan'? Statements of the jurists.
'And if he made a bequest to Banu so-and-so, women are included in it according to the first statement of Abu Hanifa and that is also the statement of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because the masculine plural encompasses women. Then he (Abu Hanifa) retracted and said: It includes only males, because the literal meaning of the word is for males, and its inclusion of women is figurative, and speech is interpreted according to its literal meaning. Contrary to the case when Banu so-and-so is the name of a tribe or sub-tribe, as then it includes males and females, because the individuals themselves are not intended, rather it is mere attribution, like Banu Adam. And for this reason, the freed slave (mawla al-itaqah), mawla al-muwalat, and their allies (hulafaa') are included.'
Translation: And if he made a bequest to Banu so-and-so, according to the first statement of Abu Hanifa and that is also the statement of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), women are included because the masculine plural encompasses women. Then Abu Hanifa retracted and said that only males are included because the literal meaning of the word is for males, and its inclusion of women is figurative, and speech is interpreted according to its literal meaning. Contrary to the case when Banu so-and-so is the name of a tribe or sub-tribe, then it includes males and females, because the individuals themselves are not intended, rather it is mere attribution, like Banu Adam. And for this reason, the freed slave (mawla al-itaqah), mawla al-muwalat, and their allies (hulafaa') are included.
Explanation: If Zaid made a bequest to Banu Khalid, now the question is whether girls are also included along with boys. There is detail: it depends whether this name refers to a tribe or the testator meant specifically the sons of Khalid. If it is a tribal name like Banu Hashim, Banu Umayyah, etc., then the testator's intent is not specifically the sons, but mere attribution, like Banu Adam, which includes all descendants, male and female. Therefore, if Banu Khalid is a tribal name, all males and females are included, and also the freed slaves (mu'tiq), mawla al-muwalat, and their successors (khulafa). If it is not a tribal name, then the statement of the two (Sahibayn) is that women are included, and this was also the first statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. But Imam Abu Hanifa's final (raj'u) statement is that women are not included; it is for males only.
The proof of the two (Sahibayn) is that the masculine plural includes women, just as 'Muslimun' includes women. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the literal meaning of 'banun' is males, and its inclusion of women is figurative, and unless there is a context (qarinah) indicating the figurative meaning, speech is interpreted literally.
Note 1: Mawla al-itaqah: for example, Banu Abbas or Banu Umayyah is an unconfined group; the slave they free will be called Banu Abbas or Banu Umayyah, i.e., attributed to that tribe, though he is not from their offspring. Mawla al-muwalat: one interpretation is what we explained in Dars Siraji; another is that a person who becomes Muslim at the hands of a tribe is counted among them and is called mawla al-muwalat. Haleef (ally): its plural is hulafaa, those who bind together by oath for mutual support.
Note 2: In Arab genealogies, the known arrangement is:
1. Sha'b (nation) which contains several tribes, e.g., Quraysh is a sha'b from Khuzaymah, under which several tribes.
Under sha'b is 'Imarah (clan), e.g., Quraysh is an 'Imarah.
Under 'Imarah are Butun (pl. of batn, belly), e.g., Qusay is a batn.
Under batn are Afkhadh (pl. of fakhdh, thigh), e.g., Hashim is a fakhdh.
Under fakhdh is Fasilah (sub-clan), e.g., Abbas is a fasilah.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion of an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of the phrase 'Banu Fulaan' (sons of so-and-so) in bequests. The key issue: when someone bequeaths to 'Banu Fulaan', are women included? There are two scenarios:

First scenario: 'Banu Fulaan' is used as a tribal name (e.g., Banu Hashim). In this case, it is a designation of lineage (intisab), not a literal reference to male children. Therefore, all members of the tribe, male and female, are included, because the word is used metaphorically for the group. Additionally, affiliated persons such as freed slaves (mawla al-itaqah), clients by alliance (mawla al-muwalat), and sworn allies (hulafaa') are also included, as they share the same attribution.

Second scenario: 'Banu Fulaan' is not a tribal name but refers literally to the sons of a named individual. Here, there is a dispute. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and the early opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa hold that women are included because the masculine plural (jama' mudhakkar) in Arabic can encompass females. Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted and held that only males are included, because the literal (haqiqi) meaning of 'banun' is male children; including women is figurative (majaz), and speech is interpreted literally unless there is a contextual indicator (qarinah sarifah) that shifts the meaning. The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is Imam Abu Hanifa's final view, that women are not included when the term is not a tribal name.

The passage then clarifies the types of affiliates: mawla al-itaqah (a freed slave whose lineage is attached to the tribe), mawla al-muwalat (a convert who affiliates with a tribe), and haleef (an ally by oath). Finally, a note on Arab genealogy hierarchy explains the levels: sha'b (nation), 'imarah (clan), batn (sub-clan), fakhdh (thigh), and fasilah (sub-sub-clan). This is background information to understand how 'Banu' works in tribal names.

Key Terms
بنون (banun): Literally 'sons' or 'male children'; in this context, the word used in bequests to mean 'descendants' or 'members of a tribe'.
مولی العتاقہ (mawla al-itaqah): A freed slave whose wala' (clientage) is attached to the tribe that freed him; he is considered part of the tribe in terms of attribution.
مولی الموالات (mawla al-muwalat): A person who enters into a clientage agreement with a tribe, often a convert who affiliates with them; he is counted among them.
حلیف / حلفاء (haleef / hulafaa): An ally bound by oath; a person who allied with a tribe for mutual support and is considered part of that group.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Zaid bequeaths to 'Banu Khalid' and Khalid is a specific person (not a tribe), according to the mufta bihi, are Khalid's daughters included?
A) Yes, because the masculine plural includes women.
B) Yes, following the Sahibayn and early Abu Hanifa.
C) No, because the literal meaning is males and there is no qarinah to shift to figurative.
D) It depends on whether the daughters are poor.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of 'Banu Fulaan' in bequests depends on whether it is a tribal name (all members included) or a literal reference (only males included per mufta bihi).

The Scope of 'Walad' in Bequests
Definition ruling on the scope of 'walad' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the term 'walad' in a bequest includes all offspring equally and apply it to distribute a bequest among heirs.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'walad' means all offspring; a bequest to 'walad fulan' is shared equally by sons and daughters.

When drafting a bequest, the choice of words matters. The term 'walad' (child) versus 'ibn' (son) leads to different distributions. This lesson clarifies that 'walad' in a bequest is gender-neutral and equally includes all children, a key distinction in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term
Locate the term 'walad' in the bequest wording. Note that it is the object of the bequest (li-waladi fulan).
The term is general; it does not specify gender or number.
2
Distinguish 'walad' from 'ibn'
Understand that 'ibn' means 'son' exclusively, while 'walad' means 'offspring' and includes both sons and daughters.
This linguistic difference is the basis of the ruling.
3
State the ruling
Al-Quduri rules that the bequest is shared among all children of the named person, with males and females receiving equal shares.
The ruling is based on the comprehensive nature of the word 'walad'.
4
Apply to a scenario
Take a concrete case: if Zaid bequeaths to 'walad Khalid', and Khalid has two sons and one daughter, the bequest is divided into three equal parts.
No son gets double; equality prevails.
5
Contrast with inheritance
Note that this rule differs from inheritance (fara'id), where sons receive double daughters. The bequest rule is specific to the wording used.
This avoids confusion with general inheritance principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اوصى لولد فلان فالوصية بينهم والذكر والانثى فيه سواء لان اسم الولد ينتظم الكل انتظاماً واحدا ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے ولد فلاں کے لئے وصیت کی تو وصیت ان کے درمیان ہوگی اور مردو عورت اس میں برابر ہوں گے اس لئے لفظ ولد سب کو شامل ہے انتظام واحد کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح ابن ، فقط بیٹا مراد ہوتا ہے اور لفظ ولد سے بیٹا اور بیٹی دونوں مراد ہوتے ہیں بالفاظ دیگر ولد حقیقتا مطلق اولا د کو شامل ہے لہذا جب زید نے ولد خالد کے لئے وصیت کی تو خالد کے لڑکے اور لڑکیاں اس وصیت میں برابر کے شریک ہوں گے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever makes a bequest to the child of so-and-so, the bequest is among them, and the male and female are equal in it, because the term 'walad' encompasses all uniformly. Translation: al-Quduri said: And whoever makes a bequest to the child of so-and-so, then the bequest will be among them, and the male and female will be equal in it, because the word 'walad' includes all with a single inclusion. Explanation: 'Ibn' only means son, but the word 'walad' means both son and daughter. In other words, 'walad' truly includes all offspring absolutely. So when Zaid made a bequest to the child of Khalid, Khalid's sons and daughters will equally share in this bequest.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It clarifies the scope of the term 'walad' (child/offspring) in bequests. Unlike 'ibn' which specifically means son, 'walad' is a general term that includes both sons and daughters. Therefore, when a testator says 'li-waladi fulan' (to the child of so-and-so), all children—male and female—receive equal shares. This is based on the linguistic principle that 'walad' covers all descendants uniformly. The Hanafi school applies this rule strictly; there is no discrimination by gender in the distribution of the bequest under this wording.

Key Terms
ولد (walad): In this passage, 'walad' means offspring, including both sons and daughters, as opposed to 'ibn' which means son only.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Zaid makes a bequest 'li-waladi Khalid', and Khalid has two sons and one daughter, how is the bequest distributed according to the Hanafi school?
A) The three children share equally
B) Sons get double the daughter
C) Only the sons receive
D) Only the daughter receives

Key Takeaway
A bequest to 'walad fulan' is shared equally by all children—sons and daughters—due to the comprehensive meaning of 'walad'.

Bequest to Heirs Follows Inheritance Shares
Ruling on bequest using 'warathah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a bequest uses the term 'warathah' and apply it to distributions involving male and female heirs.

Core Idea
Using 'warathah' in a bequest means distributing like inheritance: male takes double female.

In Hanafi law, the specific wording of a bequest matters. When a testator says 'to the heirs of so-and-so', that triggers the rules of inheritance, not equality. This lesson unpacks why the term 'warathah' leads to a 2:1 ratio between male and female recipients, a key distinction from other terms like 'walad'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative phrase
Locate the term 'warathah' (heirs) in the bequest. This is the key word that determines distribution.
2
Recognize the implication of 'warathah'
Understand that 'warathah' explicitly invokes the system of inheritance (mirath), which has fixed shares per Quran 4:11.
Contrast with 'walad' (children) which does not automatically trigger inheritance shares.
3
Apply the inheritance ratio
Distribute the bequest with males receiving twice the share of females, exactly as in inheritance.
This is the default Hanafi interpretation; no further evidence needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
در ثافلاں کے الفاظ سے وصیت کا مصداق ومن أوصى لورثة فلان فالوصية بينهم للذكور مثل حظ الأنثيين لانه لما نص على لفظ الورثة اذن ذالك بان عده التفصيل كما في الميراث ترجمہ اور جس نے فلاں کے ورثا کے لئے وصیت کی پس وصیت ان کے درمیان اللہ کر مثل حفظ الانثین کے طریقہ پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ جب اس نے لفظ در ثا کی تصریح کردی تو اس نے اس بات کی خبر دیدی کہ اس کا ارادہ تفصیل کا ہے جیسے میراث میں۔ تشریح زید نے وصیت کی کہ فلاں کے ورثا کے لئے وصیت ہے تو یہاں لڑکے اور لڑکی میں میراث کے مطابق ہزارہ ہوگا یعنی جولڑ کی کو ملے گا اس سے دو گنا لڑکے کو ملے گا اس لئے کہ لفظ ور شاکی تصریح اس کی جانب مشعر ہے کہ زید کا ارادہ یہی ہے کہ لڑکوں کا حق لڑکیوں سے زیادہ ہو جیسے میراث میں ہوتا ہے۔
The meaning of bequest with the word 'warathah'. And whoever makes a bequest to the heirs of so-and-so, the bequest is among them, for the males a share like that of two females, because when he specified the term 'warathah', that indicates that he intended detail as in inheritance. Translation: And whoever makes a bequest to the heirs of so-and-so, then the bequest among them will be on the basis of for the male the share of two females, because when he specified the term 'warathah', he informed that his intention is detail, like in inheritance. Explanation: Zaid made a bequest that it is for the heirs of so-and-so, so here between male and female the distribution will be according to inheritance, i.e., what goes to a female, the male will get double that, because the specification of the word 'warathah' indicates that Zaid's intention is that the right of males is more than females, as occurs in inheritance.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a bequest using the term 'warathah' (heirs). When a testator says 'li-warathati fulan' (to the heirs of so-and-so), the distribution follows the rules of inheritance: a male takes twice the share of a female. The rationale is that the term 'warathah' specifically invokes the concept of inheritance (mirath), which has established shares. Therefore, unlike the term 'walad' which gives equality, 'warathah' triggers the gender differential known from the Quranic inheritance laws (Surah an-Nisa, 4:11). This is a unique Hanafi position; other schools may consider the term ambiguous.

Key Terms
ورثة (warathah): Heirs; in this context, those entitled to inherit from the deceased. Using this term in a bequest implies distribution according to inheritance shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says 'I bequeath to the heirs of Amr', and Amr leaves a son and a daughter, how is the bequest distributed in Hanafi law?
A) Equally between son and daughter
B) Son gets twice the daughter
C) Daughter gets twice the son
D) Only the son receives

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to 'warathah' is distributed with males taking twice the share of females, mirroring inheritance rules.
