كتاب الوصايا
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹
غلام ورثہ کی ملک ہوتی اور خدمت بکر کے لئے ہوتی اور اس میں کوئی تعجب نہیں کیا جاتا حالانکہ یہاں بھی یہی بات ہے کہ رقبہ کسی کا اور خدمت کسی کی اور جب میراث میں یہ بات تعجب خیز بات نہ ہو گی اس لئے کہ وصیت اور میراث میں مناسبت ہے کہ دونوں کے اندر ملکیت موت کے بعد ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ حاشیہ میں اس عبارت کو حالت انفراد کی تفسیر و توضیح قرار دیا گیا ہے یعنی اگر فقط خدمت کی وصیت کرتا اور بس تو رقبہ ورثا کا ہوتا ہے اور بکر کے لئے خدمت ہوتی تو حالت انضمام میں بھی یہی اشتراک رہے گا کہ خالد کے لئے رقبہ ہوگا اور بکر کے لئے خدمت ہوگی۔ مسئلہ مذکورہ کے نظائر
ولها نظائر وهو ما اذا اوصى بامة لرجل وبما في بطنها لاخر وهى تخرج من الثلث او أوصى لرجل بخاتم والاخر بقصه او قال هذه القوصرة لفلان وما فيها من اللتمر لفلان كان كما اوصى ولا شئى لصاحب الظرف فى المظروف و في هذه المسائل كلها
ترجمہ اور اس مسئلہ کے بہت سے نظائر ہیں اور وہ یہ جب کہ موصی نے کسی شخص کے لئے باندی کی وصیت کی ہو اور دوسرے کے لئے اس کی جو اس کے پیٹ میں ہے اور باندی تہائی سے نکل جاتی ہے یا موسی نے کسی شخص کے لئے انگوٹھی کی وصیت کر دی اور دوسرے کے لئے اس کے نگینہ کی یا موصی نے کہا کہ یہ ٹوکری فلاں کے لئے ہے اور جو اس میں کھجور ہیں وہ فلاں کے لئے ہے تو ایسے ہی ہو گا جیسے موسی نے وصیت کی اور مظروف میں سے صاحب ظرف کے لئے کچھ نہ ہو گا ان تمام مسائل میں۔ تشریح شاید یہ بات آپ کو عجیب ہی اب بھی معلوم ہو کہ رقبہ غلام خالد کا اور غلام کی خدمت بکر کے لئے اس لئے مصنف نے فرمایا کہ اس مسئلہ کے بہت سے نظائر ہیں ، اب ان میں سے تین نظائر یہاں پیش فرماتے ہیں۔
زید نے وصیت کی کہ میری باندی خالد کے لئے ہے اور جو عمل اس کے پیٹ میں ہے وہ بکر کے لئے اور یہ باندی تہائی ترکہ سے نکل جاتی ہے تو باندی خالد کی ہوگی اور اس کا حمل بکر کے لئے ہوگا۔ مگر اس کے لئے یہ شرط ہے کہ حمل چھ ماہ کے اندر اندر پیدا ہو جائے ورنہ اگر چھ ماہ سے زیادہ میں بچہ پیدا ہوگا تو حمل کی وصیت صحیح نہ ہوگی ۔ (کذافی شرح الطحاوی)
- زید نے خالد کے لئے انگوٹھی کی وصیت کی اور بکر کے لئے اس کے نگینہ کی تو حلقہ خالد کا ہوگا اور نگینہ بکر کے لئے ہوگا۔ - زید نے وصیت کی کہ یہ ٹوکری خالد کے لئے وصیت ہے اور اس میں جو کھجور ہیں یہ بکر کے لئے وصیت ہیں، تو نوکری خالد کے لئے ہو گی اور کھجور بکر کیلئے ہوں گی ہیں اور باندی والے کا کوئی حصہ حمل میں نہیں نہ ہوگا، اور باندی ظرف کے درجہ میں ہے اور اس کا حمل
مظروف کے درجہ میں ہے اور ایسے ہی بقیہ دونوں مسئلوں میں صاحب ظرف ( خالد ) کا کوئی حصہ مظروف میں نہ ہوگا۔ تنبیہ اب یہاں یہ سوال باقی رہ جاتا ہے کہ اس غلام کا نفقہ کس پر واجب ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جس کے لئے خدمت کی وصیت کی گئی ہے اس پر غلام کا نفقہ واجب ہے اس لئے کہ خدمت اس وقت لینا ممکن ہے جب کہ اس پر خرچ بھی کیا جائے جیسے مئی مستعار
کا نفقہ مستعمیر پر واجب ہوتا ہے۔
اور اگر وہ غلام چھوٹا ہے جو خدمت کے قابل نہیں ہے تو قابل خدمت ہونے تک اس کا نفقہ صاحب رقبہ پر واجب ہوگا
پھر جب وہ صاحب خدمت کی خدمت کرنے لگے تو اس کا نفقہ صاحب خدمت پر واجب ہوگا۔
دود صیتوں کا اعتبار اس وقت ہے کہ دونوں موصولا ہوں، اگر مفصولاً ہوں تو کیا حکم ہے، اقوال فقہاء
اما اذا فصل احد الايجابين عن الآخر فيها فكذالك الجواب عند ابی یوسف وعلى قول محمد الامة للموصى له بها والولد بينهما نصفان و کذالک فی اخواتها ترجمہ بہر حال جب کہ موسی نے دو ایجابوں میں سے ایک کو دوسرے سے الگ کیا ہو ان تمام مسائل میں تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایسے ہی جواب ہے اور محمد کے قول کے مطابق باندی اس کے لئے جس کے لئے باندی کی وصیت کی گئی ہو اور بچہ ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا اور ایسے ہی اس کی اخوت میں ۔
تشریح ان تمام مسائل مذکورہ میں یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جب کہ دونوں وصیتوں کا ذکر موصولاً ہو۔ اور اگر مفصولاً ہو یعنی پہلے باندی کی وصیت خالد کے لئے کر دی اور پھر کلام مفصول کے ساتھ اس کے بچہ کی وصیت بکر کے لئے کر دی
تو فرمایا کہ اس میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کا اختلاف ہے۔
تو اب کیا حکم ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف اب بھی وہی فرماتے ہیں جو اصل کی صورت میں فرمایا تھا کہ باندی خالد کی ہوگی اور بچہ بکر کا ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ کلام کے مفصول ہونے کی صورت میں باندی تو اس کی ہوگی جس کے لئے باندی کی خدمت کی گئی ہے اور بچہ خالد اور بکر کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا۔ اور ان دونوں حضرات کا یہ اختلاف فقط باندی اور اس کے بچہ کے درمیان ہی نہیں ہے بلکہ خاتم اور نگینہ اور ٹوکری اور کھجور ، ان تمام مسائل میں یہی اختلاف ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل
لابي يوسف ان بايجابه فى الكلام الثانى تبين ان مراده من الكلام الاول ايجاب الامة للموصى له بهادون الولد وهذا البيان منه صحيح وان كان مفصولا لان الوصية لا تلزم شيئا في حال حيوة الموصى فكان البيان سول فيه والموصول سواء كمـ ما فى وصية الرقبة والخدمة
ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موسی نے اس ایجاب سے جو اس کے کلام ثانی میں ہے یہ بات واضح کر دی کہ کلام اول سے موصی کی مراد موصی لہ کے لئے باندی کا ایجاب ہے نہ کہ بچہ کا اور موصی کی جانب سے یہ بیان صحیح ہے اگر چہ مفصول ہے اس لئے کہ وصیت موصی کی حیات کی حالت میں کسی چیز کولازم نہیں کرتی تو اس میں بیان مفصول اور موصول برابر ہوگا جیسے رقبہ اور خدمت کی
وصیت میں ۔
تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بیان تغیر میں وصل ضروری نہیں ہے اور یہاں موصی کا کلام ثانی بیان تفسیر نہیں ہے۔ یعنی جب زید نے کلام ثانی سے بکر کے لئے ایجاب کیا تو اس کلام سے یہ بات واضح ہوگئی کہ کلام اول سے زید کی مراد فقط
Book of Bequests. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 19. The slave belongs to the heirs and his service is for Bakr, and no surprise is made in this, even though here also the same: the land (corporeal property) belongs to one and the service to another, and if in inheritance this is not surprising because there is a correspondence between bequest and inheritance: both establish ownership after death. In the margin, this phrase is taken as an explanation of the condition of singularity, meaning if he bequeaths only the service and that's it, then the corporeal property goes to the heirs and the service is for Bakr; in the condition of conjunction also the same sharing will remain: Khalid gets the corporeal property and Bakr the service. Analogues of the mentioned issue: And it has analogues: when he bequeaths a slave-girl to a man and her unborn child to another, and she is from the third; or he bequeaths a ring to a man and its stone to another; or he says: this basket is for so-and-so and what is in it of dates is for so-and-so; it is as he bequeathed and nothing of the container's owner in the contained. And in all these issues... Translation and it has many analogues: when the testator bequeaths a slave-girl to someone and her unborn child to another, and the slave-girl comes out of the third; or he bequeaths a ring to someone and its stone to another; or he says: this basket is for so-and-so and the dates in it are for so-and-so; it will be just as he bequeathed, and the owner of the container has no share in the contained. In all these issues. Explanation: Perhaps this thing still seems strange to you that the corporeal property of the slave is for Khalid and the slave's service is for Bakr; therefore the author said that this issue has many analogues. Now he presents three analogues: Zaid bequeathed that my slave-girl is for Khalid and what is in her womb is for Bakr, and this slave-girl comes out of the third of the estate; then the slave-girl will be Khalid's and her pregnancy will be for Bakr. But for this, there is a condition: the pregnancy must be born within six months; otherwise if the child is born after more than six months, the bequest of the pregnancy is not valid. (As in Sharh al-Tahawi). Zaid bequeathed the ring to Khalid and its stone to Bakr; then the ring will be Khalid's and the stone will be Bakr's. Zaid bequeathed that this basket is a bequest for Khalid and the dates in it are a bequest for Bakr; then the basket will be Khalid's and the dates will be Bakr's. And the owner of the slave-girl has no share in the pregnancy, and the slave-girl is in the status of a container and her pregnancy is in the status of the contained; and similarly in the remaining two issues, the owner of the container (Khalid) has no share in the contained. Warning: Now here a question remains: on whom is the maintenance of this slave obligatory? The answer: on the one for whom the service is bequeathed, the maintenance of the slave is obligatory, because taking service is possible only when expenditure is made on him, just as the maintenance of a borrowed item is obligatory on the borrower. And if the slave is young and not capable of service, until he becomes capable of service, his maintenance is obligatory on the owner of the corporeal property. Then when he begins to serve the one who owns the service, his maintenance becomes obligatory on the owner of the service. The consideration of two bequests is when both are connected; if they are separated, what is the ruling? Statements of the jurists: When he separates one of the two ijabs from the other in these issues, then the answer is the same according to Abu Yusuf; and according to Muhammad, the slave-girl is for the one for whom it was bequeathed, and the child is half and half between them; and similarly in its sisters. Translation: In any case, when the testator separates one of the two ijabs from the other in all these issues, then according to Abu Yusuf the answer is the same, and according to Muhammad's statement, the slave-girl is for the one for whom the slave-girl was bequeathed, and the child is half-half between them; and similarly in its parallels. Explanation: In all these mentioned issues, this ruling is when both bequests are mentioned connectedly. And if they are separated, i.e., first he bequeathed the slave-girl to Khalid, then with separated speech he bequeathed her child to Bakr, then he said: in this there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. So what is the ruling? Imam Abu Yusuf still says the same as in the original case: the slave-girl will be Khalid's and the child will be Bakr's. And Imam Muhammad says: in the case of separated speech, the slave-girl will be the one for whom the slave-girl's service was bequeathed, and the child will be half and half between Khalid and Bakr. And this disagreement of these two imams is not only between the slave-girl and her child, but it is the same in all these issues: the ring and the stone, the basket and the dates. The proof of Abu Yusuf: Abu Yusuf's proof is that by his ijab in the second speech, it becomes clear that his intention from the first speech was to make the slave-girl an ijab for the legatee without the child, and this clarification from him is valid even if it is separated, because a bequest does not make anything binding during the testator's lifetime, so the explanation in it, separated and connected, are equal, just as in the bequest of the corporeal property and service. Translation and Abu Yusuf's proof is that the testator, by this ijab which is in his second speech, made clear that from the first speech the testator's intention was the ijab of the slave-girl for the legatee, not the child; and this clarification from the testator is correct even if it is separated, because a bequest does not make anything binding during the testator's lifetime, so in this, the explanation separated and connected are equal, just as in the bequest of the corporeal property and service. Explanation: This is Imam Abu Yusuf's proof, the gist of which is that in a clarifying statement, conjunction is not necessary, and here the testator's second speech is a clarifying explanation. That is, when Zaid made an ijab for Bakr in the second speech, this speech made it clear that from the first speech Zaid intended only...
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah deals with a set of rulings concerning bequests (wasaya). The main issue is that a testator can separate ownership of a slave's corporeal property (raqabah) from the right to his service (khidmah), bequeathing each to different people. The author explains that this is not surprising because the same separation occurs in inheritance, and bequest resembles inheritance in that ownership transfers after death. The passage then provides three analogous cases to show the principle is consistent: (1) bequest of a slave-girl and her unborn child separately, (2) bequest of a ring and its stone separately, and (3) bequest of a basket and its contents separately. In each case, the 'container' (whether the slave-girl, the ring, or the basket) goes to one legatee, and the 'contained' (the child, the stone, the dates) goes to another. The child must be born within six months for the bequest to be valid, otherwise the pregnancy is treated as that of the slave-girl's owner. Then a question of maintenance (nafaqah) arises: who bears the upkeep of the slave? The answer: the one who benefits from the service must pay maintenance, similar to a borrower of a borrowed item. If the slave is too young to serve, the owner of the raqabah pays until the slave can work, then the one entitled to service takes over. Finally, the passage discusses a dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding when the two bequests are mentioned separately (munfasil) rather than together (mutasil). According to Abu Yusuf, even if the bequest of the slave-girl and the child are separated, the same ruling applies: the slave-girl goes to the first legatee, the child to the second. Muhammad, however, holds that if the bequests are separated, then the child is shared equally between the two legatees. Abu Yusuf's proof is that the testator's second statement clarifies his intention from the first, and since a bequest is not binding during his life, such a clarification is valid even when separated, just as in the preceding case of raqabah and service.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): Testamentary bequest, a disposition of property taking effect after death.
رقبہ (raqabah): The corporeal property (e.g., the slave himself) as distinct from usufruct or service.
خدمت (khidmah): Service or usufruct of a slave, bequeathable separately from the raqabah.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance and expenses (food, clothing) for the slave.
ظرف (zarf): Container; in the examples, the slave-girl, ring, or basket.
مظروف (mazruf): The contained thing; the unborn child, stone, or dates.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a ring bequeathed to Khalid and its stone to Bakr (connected speech), what is the ruling?
A) Both the ring and stone go to Khalid.
B) The ring goes to Khalid and the stone to Bakr.
C) The stone is shared equally.
D) The bequest is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In bequests, the container (zarf) and the contained (mazruf) are treated separately; the owner of the container does not automatically get the contained.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
advanced
12 min
The Dispute on Separated Bequests: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on Munfasil Wasiyyah
Commentary on the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding separated bequests.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the distribution when bequests of a container and its contents are separated (munfasil), and state the proof of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When bequests are separated, Abu Yusuf gives all to the second; Muhammad gives half to each.

This passage focuses on the difference of opinion within the Hanafi school regarding bequests that are mentioned in separate utterances (munfasil). When the testator bequeaths a slave-girl to one person in one statement, and later bequeaths her unborn child to another, do they both get their respective objects, or is the child shared? Abu Yusuf argues that the second statement clarifies the first, so the child goes entirely to the second legatee, just as in connected speech. Imam Muhammad holds that separation indicates the testator did not intend to exclude the first legatee from the child, so it is shared equally. The same dispute applies to all analogous cases like the ring and stone, basket and dates.

Guided Path
1
Recall the agreed ruling for connected (mawsul) bequests
When the testator mentions both bequests in one utterance, the container goes to one legatee and the contained to another, with no sharing.
This is the position of both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
2
Identify the dispute over separated (munfasil) bequests
The testator first says 'my slave-girl is for Khalid' and later says 'her child is for Bakr'. Abu Yusuf gives the child entirely to Bakr; Muhammad gives half to each.
The difference hinges on whether the testator's second statement is a valid clarification.
3
Analyse Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the second ijab clarifies the testator's intention: he only intended the slave-girl for Khalid, not the child. Since a bequest is not binding during life, such clarification is valid even if separated, just as in the case of raqabah and khidmah.
The principle: 'al-wasiyyah la talzim shay'an fi hal al-hayah' – a bequest does not bind during life.
4
Analyse Muhammad's reasoning
Muhammad likely argues that separation indicates the testator did not have a single intention; the first legatee of the container might also have a claim on the contained as it is naturally part of the container.
The text does not detail Muhammad's proof but states his conclusion.
5
Note the scope of the dispute
The dispute covers all analogous cases: slave-girl/child, ring/stone, basket/dates. There is no mention of tarjih (which position is relied upon).
The mufta bihi is not specified in the passage.

كتاب الوصايا
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹
غلام ورثہ کی ملک ہوتی اور خدمت بکر کے لئے ہوتی اور اس میں کوئی تعجب نہیں کیا جاتا حالانکہ یہاں بھی یہی بات ہے کہ رقبہ کسی کا اور خدمت کسی کی اور جب میراث میں یہ بات تعجب خیز بات نہ ہو گی اس لئے کہ وصیت اور میراث میں مناسبت ہے کہ دونوں کے اندر ملکیت موت کے بعد ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ حاشیہ میں اس عبارت کو حالت انفراد کی تفسیر و توضیح قرار دیا گیا ہے یعنی اگر فقط خدمت کی وصیت کرتا اور بس تو رقبہ ورثا کا ہوتا ہے اور بکر کے لئے خدمت ہوتی تو حالت انضمام میں بھی یہی اشتراک رہے گا کہ خالد کے لئے رقبہ ہوگا اور بکر کے لئے خدمت ہوگی۔ مسئلہ مذکورہ کے نظائر
ولها نظائر وهو ما اذا اوصى بامة لرجل وبما في بطنها لاخر وهى تخرج من الثلث او أوصى لرجل بخاتم والاخر بقصه او قال هذه القوصرة لفلان وما فيها من اللتمر لفلان كان كما اوصى ولا شئى لصاحب الظرف فى المظروف و في هذه المسائل كلها
ترجمہ اور اس مسئلہ کے بہت سے نظائر ہیں اور وہ یہ جب کہ موصی نے کسی شخص کے لئے باندی کی وصیت کی ہو اور دوسرے کے لئے اس کی جو اس کے پیٹ میں ہے اور باندی تہائی سے نکل جاتی ہے یا موسی نے کسی شخص کے لئے انگوٹھی کی وصیت کر دی اور دوسرے کے لئے اس کے نگینہ کی یا موصی نے کہا کہ یہ ٹوکری فلاں کے لئے ہے اور جو اس میں کھجور ہیں وہ فلاں کے لئے ہے تو ایسے ہی ہو گا جیسے موسی نے وصیت کی اور مظروف میں سے صاحب ظرف کے لئے کچھ نہ ہو گا ان تمام مسائل میں۔ تشریح شاید یہ بات آپ کو عجیب ہی اب بھی معلوم ہو کہ رقبہ غلام خالد کا اور غلام کی خدمت بکر کے لئے اس لئے مصنف نے فرمایا کہ اس مسئلہ کے بہت سے نظائر ہیں ، اب ان میں سے تین نظائر یہاں پیش فرماتے ہیں۔
زید نے وصیت کی کہ میری باندی خالد کے لئے ہے اور جو عمل اس کے پیٹ میں ہے وہ بکر کے لئے اور یہ باندی تہائی ترکہ سے نکل جاتی ہے تو باندی خالد کی ہوگی اور اس کا حمل بکر کے لئے ہوگا۔ مگر اس کے لئے یہ شرط ہے کہ حمل چھ ماہ کے اندر اندر پیدا ہو جائے ورنہ اگر چھ ماہ سے زیادہ میں بچہ پیدا ہوگا تو حمل کی وصیت صحیح نہ ہوگی ۔ (کذافی شرح الطحاوی)
- زید نے خالد کے لئے انگوٹھی کی وصیت کی اور بکر کے لئے اس کے نگینہ کی تو حلقہ خالد کا ہوگا اور نگینہ بکر کے لئے ہوگا۔ - زید نے وصیت کی کہ یہ ٹوکری خالد کے لئے وصیت ہے اور اس میں جو کھجور ہیں یہ بکر کے لئے وصیت ہیں، تو نوکری خالد کے لئے ہو گی اور کھجور بکر کیلئے ہوں گی ہیں اور باندی والے کا کوئی حصہ حمل میں نہیں نہ ہوگا، اور باندی ظرف کے درجہ میں ہے اور اس کا حمل
مظروف کے درجہ میں ہے اور ایسے ہی بقیہ دونوں مسئلوں میں صاحب ظرف ( خالد ) کا کوئی حصہ مظروف میں نہ ہوگا۔ تنبیہ اب یہاں یہ سوال باقی رہ جاتا ہے کہ اس غلام کا نفقہ کس پر واجب ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جس کے لئے خدمت کی وصیت کی گئی ہے اس پر غلام کا نفقہ واجب ہے اس لئے کہ خدمت اس وقت لینا ممکن ہے جب کہ اس پر خرچ بھی کیا جائے جیسے مئی مستعار
کا نفقہ مستعمیر پر واجب ہوتا ہے۔
اور اگر وہ غلام چھوٹا ہے جو خدمت کے قابل نہیں ہے تو قابل خدمت ہونے تک اس کا نفقہ صاحب رقبہ پر واجب ہوگا
پھر جب وہ صاحب خدمت کی خدمت کرنے لگے تو اس کا نفقہ صاحب خدمت پر واجب ہوگا۔
دود صیتوں کا اعتبار اس وقت ہے کہ دونوں موصولا ہوں، اگر مفصولاً ہوں تو کیا حکم ہے، اقوال فقہاء
اما اذا فصل احد الايجابين عن الآخر فيها فكذالك الجواب عند ابی یوسف وعلى قول محمد الامة للموصى له بها والولد بينهما نصفان و کذالک فی اخواتها ترجمہ بہر حال جب کہ موسی نے دو ایجابوں میں سے ایک کو دوسرے سے الگ کیا ہو ان تمام مسائل میں تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایسے ہی جواب ہے اور محمد کے قول کے مطابق باندی اس کے لئے جس کے لئے باندی کی وصیت کی گئی ہو اور بچہ ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا اور ایسے ہی اس کی اخوت میں ۔
تشریح ان تمام مسائل مذکورہ میں یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جب کہ دونوں وصیتوں کا ذکر موصولاً ہو۔ اور اگر مفصولاً ہو یعنی پہلے باندی کی وصیت خالد کے لئے کر دی اور پھر کلام مفصول کے ساتھ اس کے بچہ کی وصیت بکر کے لئے کر دی
تو فرمایا کہ اس میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کا اختلاف ہے۔
تو اب کیا حکم ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف اب بھی وہی فرماتے ہیں جو اصل کی صورت میں فرمایا تھا کہ باندی خالد کی ہوگی اور بچہ بکر کا ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ کلام کے مفصول ہونے کی صورت میں باندی تو اس کی ہوگی جس کے لئے باندی کی خدمت کی گئی ہے اور بچہ خالد اور بکر کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا۔ اور ان دونوں حضرات کا یہ اختلاف فقط باندی اور اس کے بچہ کے درمیان ہی نہیں ہے بلکہ خاتم اور نگینہ اور ٹوکری اور کھجور ، ان تمام مسائل میں یہی اختلاف ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل
لابي يوسف ان بايجابه فى الكلام الثانى تبين ان مراده من الكلام الاول ايجاب الامة للموصى له بهادون الولد وهذا البيان منه صحيح وان كان مفصولا لان الوصية لا تلزم شيئا في حال حيوة الموصى فكان البيان سول فيه والموصول سواء كمـ ما فى وصية الرقبة والخدمة
ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موسی نے اس ایجاب سے جو اس کے کلام ثانی میں ہے یہ بات واضح کر دی کہ کلام اول سے موصی کی مراد موصی لہ کے لئے باندی کا ایجاب ہے نہ کہ بچہ کا اور موصی کی جانب سے یہ بیان صحیح ہے اگر چہ مفصول ہے اس لئے کہ وصیت موصی کی حیات کی حالت میں کسی چیز کولازم نہیں کرتی تو اس میں بیان مفصول اور موصول برابر ہوگا جیسے رقبہ اور خدمت کی
وصیت میں ۔
تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بیان تغیر میں وصل ضروری نہیں ہے اور یہاں موصی کا کلام ثانی بیان تفسیر نہیں ہے۔ یعنی جب زید نے کلام ثانی سے بکر کے لئے ایجاب کیا تو اس کلام سے یہ بات واضح ہوگئی کہ کلام اول سے زید کی مراد فقط
Book of Bequests. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 19. The slave belongs to the heirs and his service is for Bakr, and no surprise is made in this, even though here also the same: the land (corporeal property) belongs to one and the service to another, and if in inheritance this is not surprising because there is a correspondence between bequest and inheritance: both establish ownership after death. In the margin, this phrase is taken as an explanation of the condition of singularity, meaning if he bequeaths only the service and that's it, then the corporeal property goes to the heirs and the service is for Bakr; in the condition of conjunction also the same sharing will remain: Khalid gets the corporeal property and Bakr the service. Analogues of the mentioned issue: And it has analogues: when he bequeaths a slave-girl to a man and her unborn child to another, and she is from the third; or he bequeaths a ring to a man and its stone to another; or he says: this basket is for so-and-so and what is in it of dates is for so-and-so; it is as he bequeathed and nothing of the container's owner in the contained. And in all these issues... Translation and it has many analogues: when the testator bequeaths a slave-girl to someone and her unborn child to another, and the slave-girl comes out of the third; or he bequeaths a ring to someone and its stone to another; or he says: this basket is for so-and-so and the dates in it are for so-and-so; it will be just as he bequeathed, and the owner of the container has no share in the contained. In all these issues. Explanation: Perhaps this thing still seems strange to you that the corporeal property of the slave is for Khalid and the slave's service is for Bakr; therefore the author said that this issue has many analogues. Now he presents three analogues: Zaid bequeathed that my slave-girl is for Khalid and what is in her womb is for Bakr, and this slave-girl comes out of the third of the estate; then the slave-girl will be Khalid's and her pregnancy will be for Bakr. But for this, there is a condition: the pregnancy must be born within six months; otherwise if the child is born after more than six months, the bequest of the pregnancy is not valid. (As in Sharh al-Tahawi). Zaid bequeathed the ring to Khalid and its stone to Bakr; then the ring will be Khalid's and the stone will be Bakr's. Zaid bequeathed that this basket is a bequest for Khalid and the dates in it are a bequest for Bakr; then the basket will be Khalid's and the dates will be Bakr's. And the owner of the slave-girl has no share in the pregnancy, and the slave-girl is in the status of a container and her pregnancy is in the status of the contained; and similarly in the remaining two issues, the owner of the container (Khalid) has no share in the contained. Warning: Now here a question remains: on whom is the maintenance of this slave obligatory? The answer: on the one for whom the service is bequeathed, the maintenance of the slave is obligatory, because taking service is possible only when expenditure is made on him, just as the maintenance of a borrowed item is obligatory on the borrower. And if the slave is young and not capable of service, until he becomes capable of service, his maintenance is obligatory on the owner of the corporeal property. Then when he begins to serve the one who owns the service, his maintenance becomes obligatory on the owner of the service. The consideration of two bequests is when both are connected; if they are separated, what is the ruling? Statements of the jurists: When he separates one of the two ijabs from the other in these issues, then the answer is the same according to Abu Yusuf; and according to Muhammad, the slave-girl is for the one for whom it was bequeathed, and the child is half and half between them; and similarly in its sisters. Translation: In any case, when the testator separates one of the two ijabs from the other in all these issues, then according to Abu Yusuf the answer is the same, and according to Muhammad's statement, the slave-girl is for the one for whom the slave-girl was bequeathed, and the child is half-half between them; and similarly in its parallels. Explanation: In all these mentioned issues, this ruling is when both bequests are mentioned connectedly. And if they are separated, i.e., first he bequeathed the slave-girl to Khalid, then with separated speech he bequeathed her child to Bakr, then he said: in this there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. So what is the ruling? Imam Abu Yusuf still says the same as in the original case: the slave-girl will be Khalid's and the child will be Bakr's. And Imam Muhammad says: in the case of separated speech, the slave-girl will be the one for whom the slave-girl's service was bequeathed, and the child will be half and half between Khalid and Bakr. And this disagreement of these two imams is not only between the slave-girl and her child, but it is the same in all these issues: the ring and the stone, the basket and the dates. The proof of Abu Yusuf: Abu Yusuf's proof is that by his ijab in the second speech, it becomes clear that his intention from the first speech was to make the slave-girl an ijab for the legatee without the child, and this clarification from him is valid even if it is separated, because a bequest does not make anything binding during the testator's lifetime, so the explanation in it, separated and connected, are equal, just as in the bequest of the corporeal property and service. Translation and Abu Yusuf's proof is that the testator, by this ijab which is in his second speech, made clear that from the first speech the testator's intention was the ijab of the slave-girl for the legatee, not the child; and this clarification from the testator is correct even if it is separated, because a bequest does not make anything binding during the testator's lifetime, so in this, the explanation separated and connected are equal, just as in the bequest of the corporeal property and service. Explanation: This is Imam Abu Yusuf's proof, the gist of which is that in a clarifying statement, conjunction is not necessary, and here the testator's second speech is a clarifying explanation. That is, when Zaid made an ijab for Bakr in the second speech, this speech made it clear that from the first speech Zaid intended only...
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah deals with a set of rulings concerning bequests (wasaya). The main issue is that a testator can separate ownership of a slave's corporeal property (raqabah) from the right to his service (khidmah), bequeathing each to different people. The author explains that this is not surprising because the same separation occurs in inheritance, and bequest resembles inheritance in that ownership transfers after death. The passage then provides three analogous cases to show the principle is consistent: (1) bequest of a slave-girl and her unborn child separately, (2) bequest of a ring and its stone separately, and (3) bequest of a basket and its contents separately. In each case, the 'container' (whether the slave-girl, the ring, or the basket) goes to one legatee, and the 'contained' (the child, the stone, the dates) goes to another. The child must be born within six months for the bequest to be valid, otherwise the pregnancy is treated as that of the slave-girl's owner. Then a question of maintenance (nafaqah) arises: who bears the upkeep of the slave? The answer: the one who benefits from the service must pay maintenance, similar to a borrower of a borrowed item. If the slave is too young to serve, the owner of the raqabah pays until the slave can work, then the one entitled to service takes over. Finally, the passage discusses a dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding when the two bequests are mentioned separately (munfasil) rather than together (mutasil). According to Abu Yusuf, even if the bequest of the slave-girl and the child are separated, the same ruling applies: the slave-girl goes to the first legatee, the child to the second. Muhammad, however, holds that if the bequests are separated, then the child is shared equally between the two legatees. Abu Yusuf's proof is that the testator's second statement clarifies his intention from the first, and since a bequest is not binding during his life, such a clarification is valid even when separated, just as in the preceding case of raqabah and service.

Key Terms
موصول (mawsul): Connected: the two bequests are mentioned in the same utterance without separation.
مفصول (mafsul): Separated: the two bequests are mentioned in distinct utterances.
ایجاب (ijab): The offer or declaration of bequest.
وصیت (wasiyyah): Testamentary bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if a testator bequeaths a ring to Khalid in one sentence and its stone to Bakr in a later sentence, how is the stone distributed?
A) Entirely to Khalid.
B) Entirely to Bakr.
C) Half to Khalid and half to Bakr.
D) The bequest is invalid.

Key Takeaway
When bequests of a container and its contents are separated (munfasil), Abu Yusuf gives the contained entirely to the second legatee, while Muhammad shares it equally; the mufta bihi is not specified in this text.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Multiple Bequests of a Ring: Sharing vs Revocation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequests of parts of a ring

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple bequests of a ring and its stone, explain why Imam Muhammad rejected Abu Yusuf's analogy, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the two positions.

Core Idea
A later bequest of the ring does not revoke an earlier bequest of its stone—the stone is shared, because the ring includes the stone.

How should we resolve a will that first gives away the stone of a ring, and later gives away the entire ring? Does the second bequest cancel the first, or do they coexist? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi debate between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf, and shows how the Hanafi school resolved it using meticulous analysis of language and analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the two positions
State the exact scenario: testator bequeaths the stone (fass) to one person, then the ring (khatam) to another. Note the two possible outcomes: sharing the stone, or the second bequest revoking the first.
The passage explicitly mentions both possibilities and favours sharing.
2
Understand Abu Yusuf's analogy to body and service
Examine why Abu Yusuf argued for revocation: he analogized to a slave's body and service. If body is bequeathed first and service later, the second revokes because body does not include service.
Key: the illa is that the later bequest covers the same subject (the slave's service) which was not included in the first.
3
Analyse Imam Muhammad's rebuttal (qiyas ma'a al-fariq)
Imam Muhammad rejects the analogy because 'ring' includes 'stone', unlike 'body' which does not include 'service'. Therefore, the second bequest is for the ring alone, not the stone, and the stone remains with the first legatee.
This is a classic case of qiyas ma'a al-fariq – an invalid analogy due to a fundamental difference.
4
Determine the operative ruling and practical difference
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Imam Muhammad's: the stone is shared if both bequests are for the stone; but if stone is first and ring later, the stone belongs solely to the first legatee and the ring (band) is common. Under Abu Yusuf, the later bequest would give the entire ring to the second legatee.
The thamarah al-khilaf: the second legatee gets only the band (not the stone) in the mufta bihi view.

وصیتیں ہیں اور دونوں الگ الگ ایجاب سے ثابت ہوئی ہیں تو اب یہاں دو صورتیں ہیں: نگینہ کو ان دونوں کے درمیان مشترک قرار دیدیا جائے۔ دوسرے ایجاب کو اول سے رجوع قراردے دیا جائے۔ مگر یہاں ثانی طریقہ تو مناسب نہیں بلکہ اول طریقہ انسب ہے لہذا اس پر عمل کیا گیا ہے اور اس کو اول سے رجوع قرار نہیں دیا گیا ہے۔ ا جیسے اگر موصی خالد کے لئے نگینہ کی وصیت کرے اور پھر بکر کے لئے خاتم کی وصیت کرے تو اب بھی نگینہ فقط خالد کا ہو گا اور حلقہ ان دونوں کے درمیان مشترک ہوگا۔ امام محمد کی طرف سے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب بخلاف الخدمة مع الرقبة لان اسم الرقبة لا يتناول الخدمة وانما يستخدمه الموصى له بحكم ان المنفعة حصلت على ملكه فإذا أوجب الخدمة لغيره لا يبقى للموصى له فيه حق بخلاف ما اذا كان الكلام موصولاً لان ذالك دليل التخصيص والاستثناء فتبين انه اوجب لصاحب الخاتم الحلقة خاصة دون الفص ترجمه بخلاف خدمت کے رقبہ کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ لفظ رقبہ خدمت کو شامل نہیں ہے اور موصی لہ اس سے خدمت لیتا ہے اس حکم سے که منفعت موصی لہ کی ملک پر حاصل ہوئی ہے پس جب موصی نے اس کے غیر کے لئے خدمت کا ایجاب کیا تو خدمت میں موصی لڑکا کوئی حق باقی نہیں رہا۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ کلام موصول ہو اس لئے کہ تخصیص اور استثناء کی دلیل ہے تو یہ بات واضح ہو گئی کہ صاحب خاتم نے خصوصیت سے حلقہ کا ایجاب کیا ہے نہ کہ نگینہ کا۔ تشریح یہ امام محمد کی طرف سے امام ابو یوسف کا جواب ہے امام ابو یوسف نے مسائل ثلاثہ مذکورہ کور قبہ اور خدمت کے مسئلہ پر قیاس کیا تھا تو امام محمد نے جواب دیا کہ یہ قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ کیونکہ خاتم تو نگینہ کو شامل ہے اور باندی کے اندر کا حصہ بھی داخل ہے مگر رقبہ میں خدمت شامل نہیں ہے۔ سوال تو پھر جس شخص کے لئے غلام کی وصیت کی گئی ہو اور کسی دوسرے شخص کے لئے اس کی خدمت کی وصیت نہ کی گئی ہو وہ خدمت لینے کا مستحق کیوں ہوتا ہے؟ جواب ... اس موصی لہ کو جو خدمت لینے کا حق ہوا ہے اس بنا پر نہیں ہوا کہ رقبہ خدمت کو شامل ہے بلکہ اس بنا پر ہوا ہے کہ یہاں منافع خدمت موصی لیا کی ملکیت پر حاصل ہوں گے۔ لیکن جب موصی نے خدمت کا ایجاب دوسرے شخص کے لئے کر دیا تو اب خدمت میں پہلے موصی لہ کا حق نہیں رہا۔ اور یہاں اشتراک کے قول کو اختیار نہیں کیا گیا کیونکہ رقبہ پہلے ہی سے خدمت کو شامل نہیں ہے لہذا ہم نے کہا کہ رقبہ پہلے موصی له کے لئے ہوگا اور خدمت دوسرے موصی لا کے لئے ہوگی۔ اور اگر مقیس میں دوسرا ایجاب موصول ہو تو اس بیان کو دلیل خصوص اور استثناء کے درجہ میں رکھا جائے گا جس کا واضح مطلب یہ ہے کہ موسی نے پہلے ہی سے خالد کے لئے پوری انگوٹھی کا ایجاب نہیں کیا بلکہ صرف حلقہ کا کیا ہے نگینہ کا نہیں کیا ہے۔
The acceptance of the bequest for the second is a revocation of the first, just as when he bequeaths the ring to the second. Translation: So two bequests are combined in the stone, and each of them is with a separate acceptance, so the stone will be divided half and half between them, and the bequest's acceptance for the second will not be a revocation of the first, as when the testator bequeaths the ring to the second. Elaboration: This is further explanation of the first statement: here there are two bequests regarding the stone, and both are established by separate acceptances. Now there are two possibilities: 1) The stone is declared common between them. 2) The second acceptance is declared a revocation of the first. But the second method is not suitable; rather the first method is more appropriate, so it is acted upon, and it is not declared a revocation of the first. For example, if the testator bequeaths the stone to Khalid and then bequeaths the ring to Bakr, even then the stone will be only Khalid's, and the ring will be common between them. The response of Imam Muhammad to the proof of Imam Abu Yusuf: Contrary to the service with the body, because the word 'body' does not include service, and the legatee takes service by virtue that the benefit is acquired into his ownership. So when he causes the service to be accepted for another, the legatee has no right left in it, contrary to the case when the speech is connected, because that is evidence of specification and exception, so it becomes clear that he caused the acceptance of the ring-owner specifically for the ring, not for the stone. Translation: Unlike service with the body, because the word 'body' does not include service, and the legatee takes service from it by virtue that the benefit is acquired into his ownership. So when the testator causes the service to be accepted for another, the legatee has no right left in service. Contrary to the case when the speech is connected, because that is evidence of specification and exception, so it becomes clear that the owner of the ring caused acceptance specifically for the ring, not for the stone. Elaboration: This is the response of Imam Muhammad to Imam Abu Yusuf. Imam Abu Yusuf had analogized the mentioned three issues to the issue of the dome and service. Imam Muhammad replied that this analogy is invalid (ma'a al-fariq) because the ring includes the stone, and the slave girl's part is also included, but the body does not include service. Question: Then why is the person for whom a slave is bequeathed, and no bequest of his service is made to another, entitled to take service? Answer: The right of the legatee to take service is not because the body includes service, but because here the benefits of service will be acquired into the legatee's ownership. But when the testator causes the service to be accepted for another person, then the first legatee has no right left in service. And here the opinion of sharing is not adopted because the body does not already include service, so we said that the body will be for the first legatee and the service for the second legatee. And if in the analogized case the second acceptance is connected, then that statement is placed as evidence of specification and exception, the clear meaning of which is that the testator did not cause the acceptance of the entire ring for Khalid from the beginning, but rather only the ring, not the stone.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning multiple bequests of parts of a ring. The ruling states: if a testator bequeaths the stone (fass) of a ring to one person and then the entire ring (khatam) to another, the stone is shared equally between the two legatees; the second bequest does not revoke the first. The passage explains two possible outcomes: sharing or revocation, and declares sharing more appropriate. It then provides an example where bequest of the stone to Khalid and the ring to Bakr results in the stone being solely for Khalid and the ring common. Imam Muhammad responds to Abu Yusuf's earlier analogy comparing this to the case of a slave's body and service. The response distinguishes that the word 'body' does not include 'service', whereas 'ring' includes 'stone'. When the testator bequeaths service to someone else, the first legatee loses his right to service. Conversely, in the ring case, since 'ring' includes 'stone', a second bequest of the ring implies the ring (excluding the stone) is bequeathed, so the stone remains with the first legatee. Imam Muhammad thus rejects Abu Yusuf's analogy as invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Key Terms
ایاب (ijab): Acceptance of the bequest by the legatee, which establishes the right.
رجوع (ruju'): Revocation; the second bequest nullifying the first.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because of a fundamental difference between the two cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, if Zayd bequeaths the stone of his ring to 'Amr and then later bequeaths the entire ring to Bakr, what happens?
A) The second bequest revokes the first, so Bakr gets the entire ring including the stone.
B) The stone is shared equally between 'Amr and Bakr.
C) 'Amr gets the stone, and Bakr gets the ring (excluding the stone).
D) The bequests are invalid due to conflict.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a testator bequeaths the stone of a ring and then the ring itself, the second bequest does not revoke the first; the stone belongs to the first legatee, and the second legatee receives the ring (without the stone) as per Imam Muhammad's relied-upon position.

Bequest of Fruit vs. Produce: The Role of Custom (Urf)
Ruling with rationale on what is included in bequest of fruit and produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the legal scopes of 'thamar' and 'ghallah' in a bequest and explain how custom (urf) determines the inclusion of future yields.

Core Idea
Custom gives 'fruit' only existing, 'produce' includes future – a single word changes everything.

In Hanafi bequest law, the terms a testator uses carry precise legal consequences. This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir illustrates how the word 'fruit' (thamar) and 'produce' (ghallah) have different scopes, and how adding 'forever' or using 'ghallah' expands the bequest to future yields. The distinction rests on customary usage (urf), a foundational principle in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three bequest scenarios: (1) bequest of 'fruit' without qualification, (2) bequest of 'fruit' with 'forever', (3) bequest of 'produce' without qualification.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For each scenario, state what the legatee receives: only existing fruit, both existing and future fruit, or both existing and future produce.
The ruling depends on the wording and the term used.
3
Compare the scope of 'thamar' vs 'ghallah'
Analyze why 'thamar' needs an explicit extension (like 'forever') to include future yields, while 'ghallah' inherently includes them. This is based on customary usage.
Custom is the key: 'thamar' is customarily only the existing fruit, while 'ghallah' customarily includes recurring income.
4
Understand the legal rationale (talil)
The passage explains: 'thamar' in custom is a name for what exists, so it does not include non-existent unless specified. 'Ghallah' encompasses what exists and what is about to come into existence repeatedly. Recognize that this is a rule of interpretation based on 'urf'.
This rationale is rooted in the Hanafi reliance on customary meaning.
5
Apply the principle of 'urf' to a new case
Consider if a testator bequeaths 'the dates of my palm tree' without further qualification. What does the legatee receive? Apply the custom: dates are fruit, so only existing dates at death are included unless 'forever' is added.
Think about how custom defines the scope of similar terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اوصى لاخر بثمرة بستانه ثم مات و فيه ثمرة فله هذه الثمرة وحدها وان قال له ثمرة بستانی ابداً فله هذه الثمرة وثمرته فيما يستقبل ما عاش و ان اوصى له بغلة بستانه فله الغلة القائمة و غلته فيما يستقبل ترجمہ امام احمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور جس نے دوسرے کے لئے اپنے باغ کے پھل کی وصیت کی پھر موصی مر گیا اور باغ میں پھل ہیں تو اس کے لئے فقط یہی پھل ہوگا اور اگر موصی نے کہا ہو کہ اس کے لئے ہمیشہ میرے باغ کا پھل ہے تو موصی لا کے لئے یہ پھل ہوگا اور اس باغ کا آئندہ پھل ہو گا جب تک کہ موسی زندہ رہے اور گر موسی نے موصی لہ کے لئے اپنے باغ کی آمدنی کی وصیت کی تو موصی لا کیلئے موجودہ آمدنی اور اس کی آئندہ کی آمدنی ہوگی ۔ تشریح زید نے خالد کے لئے اپنے باغ کے پھل کی وصیت کی تو موصی کے موت کے وقت جو پھل ہے خالد فقط اس کا مستحق ہوگا اور جو آئندہ پھل آئے گا اس کا مستحق نہ ہوگا اور اگر خالد کے لئے اس نے اپنے باغ کے پھل کی وصیت ہمیشہ کے لئے کردی تو جو پچھل بوقت موت موصی ہے وہ بھی داخل ہے اور جو آئندہ پھل آئے گا وہ بھی داخل ہوگا اور موصی لہ کی حیات تک باغ کا پھل موصی لیہ کو مانتا رہے گا۔ اور اگر زید نے بجائے پھل کے آمدنی کہا ہو تو پھر بغیر لفظ ابد کے موجودہ آمدنی اور آئندہ کی آمدنی وصیت میں داخل ہو جائے گی جب تک کہ خالد زندہ ہے۔ شمرہ اور غلہ کے فرق کی وجہ والفرق ان الثمرة اسم للموجود عرفا فلا يتناول المعدوم الابد لالة زائدة مثل التنصيص على الابد لانه لا يتابد الابتناول المعدوم والمعدوم مذكور وان لم يكن شيئا اما الغلة تنتظم الموجود وما يكون بعرض الوجود مرة بعد أخرى ترجمہ اور وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ شمر عرفا موجود کا نام ہے پس وہ معدوم کو شامل نہ ہو گا مگر دلالت زائدہ کی وجہ سے جیسے اہد پر تصریح کردینا اس لئے کہ پھل تا بیدی نہ ہوگا مگر معدوم کو شامل ہونے کے ساتھ اور معدوم قابل ذکر ہے اگر چہ وہ چھٹی نہیں ہے بہر حال لفظ غلہ شامل ہے موجود کو اور اس کو جو یکے بعد دیگرے وجود کی صلاحیت رکھتے عرفا۔
He said: And whoever bequeaths to another the fruit of his garden, then dies and there is fruit in it, then he has this fruit alone. And if he said to him: the fruit of my garden forever, then he has this fruit and its fruit in the future as long as he lives. And if he bequeaths to him the produce of his garden, then he has the existing produce and its produce in the future. Translation: Imam Ahmad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And whoever bequeaths to another the fruit of his garden, then the testator dies and there are fruits in the garden, then for him (the legatee) is only this fruit. And if the testator said that for him is the fruit of my garden forever, then for the legatee is this fruit and the future fruit of that garden as long as the testator lives. And if the testator bequeaths to the legatee the income of his garden, then for the legatee is the existing income and its future income. Elaboration: Zayd bequeaths to Khalid the fruit of his garden. So at the time of the testator's death, the fruit that exists, Khalid is only entitled to it, and he is not entitled to future fruit. And if he bequeaths to Khalid the fruit of his garden forever, then the fruit existing at the time of death is included, and future fruit is also included, and the fruit of the garden continues to be given to the legatee as long as he lives. And if Zayd said 'income' instead of fruit, then without the word 'forever', existing income and future income are included in the bequest as long as Khalid lives. The reason for the difference between fruit (thamar) and produce (ghallah): And the difference is that 'thamar' in custom is a name for what exists, so it does not include non-existent except by an additional indication, like specifying 'forever', because it does not last forever except by including non-existent, and non-existent is mentionable even if it is not a thing. But 'ghallah' encompasses what exists and what is about to come into existence time after time. Translation: And the reason for the difference is that 'thamar' is customarily a name for what exists, so it does not include non-existent except by an additional indication, like explicit mention of 'forever', because fruit does not continue perpetually except by including non-existent, and non-existent is mentionable even if it is not a thing. Anyway, the word 'ghallah' includes what exists and that which is susceptible to coming into existence one after another customarily.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad regarding bequest of fruit (thamar) and produce (ghallah) of a garden. The ruling distinguishes three scenarios: (1) If a testator bequeaths 'the fruit of my garden' without qualification, only the fruit existing at the time of death is included. (2) If he adds 'forever', then both existing and future fruit during the legatee's lifetime are included. (3) If he bequeaths 'the produce (ghallah) of my garden', then both existing and future produce are included without needing the word 'forever'. The passage then explains the legal rationale: the word 'thamar' customarily refers to what exists, so it does not extend to future fruit unless specified. The word 'ghallah', however, customarily includes both existing and recurring yields. This is an important distinction in Hanafi bequest law based on linguistic custom (urf).

Key Terms
ثمرة (thamar): Fruit of a garden; customarily refers to existing fruit only.
غلة (ghallah): Produce or income; includes both existing and future yields.
عرف (urf): Customary usage; determines the scope of terms in bequests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Zayd bequeaths 'the fruit of my garden' to Khalid without adding 'forever', what does Khalid receive?
A) Only the fruit existing at Zayd's death
B) The fruit existing at death plus future fruit
C) The fruit existing at death and for one year
D) The entire garden

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi bequest law, the term 'fruit' (thamar) is limited to existing fruit, while 'produce' (ghallah) includes future yields, based on customary usage (urf).

Bequest of Sheep Products: Existing Items Only
Ruling that bequest of sheep products includes only what exists at death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequest of wool, offspring, and milk, and explain why 'forever' does not expand the bequest beyond what exists at death.

Core Idea
For wool, offspring, and milk, only what exists at death is bequeathed — 'forever' adds nothing.

In the previous lesson, we saw that bequeathing fruit with the word 'forever' could include future yields. Here, Imam Muhammad presents a contrasting rule for animal products: wool, offspring, and milk. The key difference hinges on the nature of the property — these are separable items that exist at death and are not renewed like fruit. Let's examine the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest and its scope
The testator bequeaths wool, offspring, or milk 'forever'. Determine whether the legatee gets only current items or future ones as well.
The phrase 'forever' (abadan) is explicitly considered.
2
Extract the Hanafi ruling
From the text: 'falahu ma fi butuniha min al-walad wa ma fi duru'iha min al-laban wa ma 'ala zuhuriha min al-suf yawma yamutu al-musi.' The legatee takes only what exists at death.
Regardless of 'abadan'.
3
Analyze the talil (reasoning)
The author states: 'li-annahu ijab 'ind al-mawt fa-yu'tabaru qiyam hadhihi al-ashya' yawma'idhin.' The bequest is an obligation at death, so only existing items count.
This contrasts with the earlier ruling on fruit.
4
Understand the contrast with fruit
Why does 'abadan' work for fruit but not for these? Because fruit is a recurring yield (ghalla), while wool, offspring, and milk are specific items that exist at a point in time.
Future fruit is considered a future benefit; future shearing or lambing is not.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario: testator bequeaths 'the milk of my goats forever' and dies. The legatee gets only the milk in the udders at death, not future milk.
The same applies to wool and offspring.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن أوصى لرجل بصوف غنمه ابداً او باولادها او بلبنها ثم مات فله ما في بطونها من الولد وما في ضروعها من اللبن وما على ظهورها من الصوف يوم يموت الموصى سواء قال ابدا اولم يقل لانه ايجاب ند الموت فيعتبر قيام هذه الاشياء يومئذ وهذا بخلاف ما تقدم
He said: Whoever bequeaths to a man the wool of his sheep forever, or their offspring, or their milk, then dies, then for him (the legatee) is what is in their wombs of offspring, what is in their udders of milk, and what is on their backs of wool on the day the testator dies, whether he said 'forever' or not, because it is a bequest at the time of death, so the existence of these things is considered at that time. And this is contrary to what preceded.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the same source (al-Jami' al-Saghir) regarding bequests of animal products like wool, offspring, and milk. Unlike the case of fruit (thamara) where future yields could be included with the word 'abadan', here the legatee only receives what is physically present at the testator's death—regardless of whether 'abadan' is used. The reason given is that this bequest takes effect at death (wasiyyah), so only the existing items are considered. The ruling contrasts with the previous one: for fruit, 'abadan' could expand the bequest to future fruit; for these animal products, 'abadan' has no such effect. This is because wool, offspring, and milk are considered to be 'ayn (specific, identifiable items) that are separable, whereas fruit is a periodic crop. The Hanafi position is that the default for such bequests is what exists at death; future growth (like next shearing or next lambing) is not included even if 'abadan' is specified, because the bequest is an ijab 'ind al-mawt (transaction at death) and the property vests immediately, so future products belong to the heirs unless explicitly bequeathed with a different wording like 'ghalla' (income).

Key Terms
صوف (suf): Wool; the wool on the sheep's back at the testator's death is bequeathed.
ولد (walad): Offspring; unborn young in the womb at the testator's death are included.
لبن (laban): Milk; milk in the udder at the testator's death is bequeathed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what effect does saying 'forever' (abadan) in a bequest of sheep wool have?
A) It expands the bequest to include future wool each shearing.
B) It has no effect; the legatee still only gets the wool at death.
C) It makes the bequest invalid because indefinite.
D) It doubles the amount of wool received.

Key Takeaway
In a bequest of wool, offspring, or milk, only the items physically present at the testator's death are transferred, regardless of the word 'forever'.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate

Will for Perpetual Wool, Milk, and Offspring: Only Existing Items Included
Explaining the scope of perpetual wills for animal products

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a will for future wool, milk, or offspring covers only items existing at death, and explain the distinction from fruits and produce.

Core Idea
A perpetual will for wool, milk, or offspring covers only what exists at death—future items are excluded due to no Shari'ah exception.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah clarifies a subtle point about wills for future animal produce. It distinguishes between items like fruits (which can be willed for future yields due to Shari'ah exceptions like musaqah) and animal products like wool, milk, and offspring (which cannot). The ruling turns on the principle that a will takes effect at death, and only then-existing property can be transferred unless a specific Shari'ah permission exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the will scenario
Recognize that the testator makes a perpetual will (saying 'forever') for the wool, milk, or offspring of his goats.
The word 'forever' does not change the ruling.
2
State the ruling
Only the items existing at the testator's death are included—wool on the back, milk in the udder, offspring in the womb at that moment.
This is based on the principle that a will takes effect at death (ijab at death).
3
Contrast with fruits and produce
For fruits (thamarah) and produce (ghallah), the Shari'ah permits contracts (musaqah/Ijara) on nonexistent items, so a will for them can include future items if the word 'forever' is added.
This is an exception to the general rule.
4
Understand the 'illa (effective cause)
The 'illa is the existence of a Shari'ah exception for fruits and produce. Since wool, milk, and offspring have no such exception, they remain under the general prohibition of owning nonexistent items.
The qiyas uses istihsan (hidden analogy) overriding the general qiyas.

سوال پھل اور آمدنی بھی تو معدوم ہیں حالانکہ آمدنی میں آپ نے بغیر ابد کی صراحت کے اور پھل میں ابد کی صراحت کے ساتھ آ نے اس کو معدوم پر مشتمل مان لیا ہے؟
جواب قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہی ہے مگر کیا کیا جائے مساقات اور اجارہ کے متعلق شریعت وارد ہوگئی اور شریعت نے اس کو جائز قرار دے دیا اور پھل میں وہی مساقات کا مسئلہ ہے اور آمدنی میں اجارہ کا اس لئے ان دونوں میں معدوم ہونے کے باوجود جب شریعت نے ان کو جائز قرار دیدیا تو ان کی وصیت کا جواز بدرجہ اولی ثابت ہوگا اس لئے کہ باب وصیت وسیع ہے اور اون اور دودھ اور بکری کی اولاد جو معدوم ہوں یہ سب ایسی چیزیں ہیں جن پر معدوم ہونے کی صورت میں کوئی عقد نہیں ہو سکتا اور نہ کسی عقد سے ان کا استحقاق ثابت ہوسکتا اس لئے یہ وصیت کے تحت بھی داخل نہیں ہو سکتے البتہ ان اشیاء ثلاثہ میں سے جو چیزیں موجود ہیں تو ان کا عقد بیع کے ضمن میں تبعاً استحقاق ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ مثلا کسی نے بکری خریدی تو تبعا اس کی اون دودھ اور اس کا بچہ بھی بیچ میں داخل ہو گیا۔ اور عقد خلع میں قصداً ان کا استحقاق ہو سکتا ہے۔ مثلاً کسی عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے کہا کہ میری باندی یا میری بکری کے پیٹ میں جو کچھ ہے اس کے بدلہ مجھ سے ضلع کر لیجئے اور شوہر نے قبول کیا تو ضلع صحیح ہو گیا اور جو بکری کے پیٹ میں ہے وہی شوہر کو ملے گا تو جب یہ اشیاء ثلاثہ جب کہ موجود ہوں تبعا بیچ میں داخل ہو سکتی ہیں اور ضلع میں قصداً پس وصیت میں بھی داخل ہوں گی اور ان کی وصیت کرنا صحیح ہوگا۔
Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whoever makes a will for someone of the wool of his goats forever, or of their offspring, or of their milk, then the testator dies — for the legatee is that which is in their wombs, that milk which is in their udders, and that wool which is on their backs on the day the testator died, whether he said 'forever' or not. Because this will is an ijab at the time of death, so consideration is given to the existence of these items on that day. This is contrary to the earlier issue. Commentary: Zaid made a will for Khalid that Khalid will always receive the wool of his goats, or their milk, or their offspring that are born. So Khalid only gets the wool, offspring, and milk that exists at the time of Zaid's death, whether Zaid added the condition of perpetuity or not. Because the will is considered an ijab only at death, so existence is considered on that day only, not afterward. This is unlike the issue of fruits and produce where produce is inherently perpetual, and fruits, though not inherently perpetual, become perpetual if the condition of perpetuity is added. But here perpetuity does not occur in any way. The difference: Qiyas rejects the ownership of a nonexistent thing because it cannot accept ownership. However, for nonexistent fruits and produce, the Shari'ah has allowed contracts upon them, such as musaqah and ijara. So this necessitates the permissibility of a will regarding them by primary analogy because the chapter of wills is broader. As for nonexistent offspring and its two sisters (wool and milk), it is not permissible to enter a contract upon them at all, nor can they be acquired by contract. Thus they do not enter under the will, unlike the existent ones because it is permissible to acquire them by a sale contract as a subsidiary, and by a khul' contract as a primary object, so likewise by will. Commentary: Here the reason is given why wool, milk, and offspring do not include future items even with the explicit mention of 'forever', while fruits and produce include future items after adding 'forever'. So he said: The requirement of qiyas is that a nonexistent thing cannot be owned because it does not accept ownership, so how can one make someone else its owner? Question: Fruits and produce are also nonexistent, yet you considered that produce includes nonexistent without the condition of 'forever', and fruits include nonexistent with the condition of 'forever'? Answer: The requirement of qiyas is this, but what can be done? The Shari'ah has come regarding musaqah and ijara and declared them permissible. Fruit is the issue of musaqah, and produce is the issue of ijara. So when the Shari'ah has permitted them despite being nonexistent, the permissibility of a will regarding them is proven by primary analogy because the chapter of wills is broad. As for wool, milk, and offspring that are nonexistent, these are things upon which no contract can be made when they are nonexistent, nor can their entitlement be established by any contract. Therefore they cannot enter under the will. However, of these three things, that which exists can be acquired by a sale contract as a subsidiary. For example, if someone buys a goat, its wool, milk, and offspring are also included in the sale as a subsidiary. And by a khul' contract, they can be acquired as a primary object. For example, a woman said to her husband, 'Divorce me in exchange for what is in the womb of my slave-girl or my goat,' and the husband accepted, then the khul' is valid and whatever is in the goat's womb goes to the husband. So when these three things exist, they can enter into a sale as a subsidiary and into khul' as a primary object, so they will also enter into a will, and making a will for them is valid.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof and qiyas reasoning from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. The author explains the ruling that if someone makes a perpetual will for the wool, milk, or offspring of his goats, only what exists at the time of the testator's death is included, regardless of whether he used the word 'forever'. The reason is that the will takes effect only at death, so only items existing at that moment are considered. This differs from the earlier case of fruits and produce, where perpetuity can be achieved. The proof is based on qiyas and istihsan: Qiyas generally forbids ownership of nonexistent items because they cannot own. However, the Shari'ah has allowed contracts like musaqah (for fruit) and ijara (for produce) on future items, so by primary analogy, wills for these are even more permissible since the chapter of wills is broader. For wool, milk, and offspring, no such Shari'ah exception exists. They cannot be the subject of any contract when nonexistent. Therefore, they are not included in the will. However, if they exist at the time of death, they can be acquired through sale as a subsidiary (taba'an) or through khul' as a primary object, so they can be included in a will.

Key Terms
معدوم (ma'dum): That which does not exist at the time of the contract or will; a nonexistent item that cannot be owned directly according to qiyas.
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; the act of making someone owner of a thing.
استحقاق (istihqaq): Entitlement or right to receive a thing; can be primary (qasdan) or subsidiary (taba'an).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All wool that will grow forever, because 'perpetual' means continuous ownership.
B) Only the wool that exists on the goats' backs at the time of the testator's death.
C) Only the wool that is sheared during the testator's lifetime.
D) None, because goats' wool cannot be willed.

Key Takeaway
A perpetual will for wool, milk, or offspring covers only items existing at testator's death, unlike fruits and produce which include future yields due to Shari'ah exceptions.

The Dhimmi's Place of Worship: Inheritance or Invalid?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inheritance of a dhimmi's built place of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a dhimmi's built church/synagogue becomes inheritance, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of this dispute.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's church becomes inheritance like waqf (Abu Hanifa); Sahibayn deem it invalid as disobedience.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a dhimmi who builds a church or synagogue during his health and then dies. The disagreement centers on whether the building is analogous to a waqf (endowment) that is inheritable under Abu Hanifa's view, or an act of disobedience (ma'siyah) that renders the building invalid according to the Sahibayn. We will unpack the reasoning on both sides and see how the practical outcome differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is a dhimmi building a place of worship (church or synagogue) during his life, then dying. The dispute is whether this building becomes part of the estate (inheritance) or is invalid.
The building is a physical asset; the question is its legal status after death.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his analogy
Abu Hanifa rules that the building is inheritance. He analogizes it to a waqf: just as a waqf according to him is inheritable (not binding), this building is inheritable.
Abu Hanifa's view on waqf: it is revocable and passes to heirs.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their basis
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that building a place of worship for disbelief is an act of disobedience (ma'siyah), so the building is not validly made as a waqf or as any valid transaction; thus it cannot be inherited.
Ma'siyah: an act contrary to the Sharī'ah; here, facilitating kufr worship.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the building is distributed among heirs as part of the estate. Under Sahibayn, the building is not validly owned by the deceased, so it may remain as abandoned property or be disposed of differently.
The commentary states 'it becomes inheritance' indicating the applied view is Abu Hanifa's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب وصية الذمى
ترجمہ یہ باب ذمی کی وصیت کا ہے
تشریح مسلمانوں کی وصیت کے احکام بیان کرنے کے بعد اب مصنف ذمی کی وصیت کے احکام بیان کر رہے ہیں اس لئے کہ کفار معاملات کے حق میں مسلمانوں کے تابع ہیں ۔
( وفیہ کلام فی النتائج) یہودی کا بنایا ہوا کنیسہ اور نصرانی کا بنایا ہوا بیعہ ان کے مرنے کے بعد میراث بن جائے گا ، اقوال فقہاء
قال و اذا صنع یهودی او نصرانى بيعة او كنيسة فى صحته ثم مات فهو ميراث لان هذا بمنزلة الوقف عند ابي حنيفة والوقف عنده يورث لا يلزم فكذا هذا واما عندهما فلان هذه معصية فلا تصح عندهما
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جب کہ یہودی یا نصرانی نے بیعہ یا کنیسہ بنایا اپنی صحت کی حالت میں پھر وہ مر گیا تو وہ میراث ہے اس لئے کہ حنیفہ کے نزدیک وقف کے درجہ میں ہے اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وقف میراث ہوتا ہے اور لازم نہیں ہوتا پس ایسے ہی یہ ہو گا اور بہر حال صاحبین کے نزدیک پس اس لئے کہ یہ معصیت ہے تو ان کے نزدیک صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح کسی یہودی نے کنیسہ ( اپنا عبادت گھر ) اور کسی نصرانی نے بیعہ (اپنا عبادت گھر ) اپنی صحت کی حالت میں بنایا اور پھر وہ یہودی یا نصرانی مرگیا تو یہ بیعہ یا کنیسہ میراث ہو کر جانے والے کے ورثا کے درمیان تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔
Translation: Chapter on the will of a dhimmi. Commentary: After explaining the rulings of Muslims' wills, the author now explains the rulings of a dhimmi's will because the disbelievers follow Muslims in transactional matters. (And it contains discussion of conclusions). A Jew's built synagogue or a Christian's built church becomes inheritance after they die. Statements of jurists: He (Muhammad) said: If a Jew or Christian built a church or synagogue during his health, then he died, it is inheritance. Because this is like a waqf according to Abu Hanifa, and with him waqf is inheritable and not binding, so this is the same. As for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because this is an act of disobedience, so it is not valid according to them. Commentary: If a Jew built a synagogue (his place of worship) or a Christian built a church (his place of worship) during his health, and then that Jew or Christian died, this church or synagogue becomes inheritance and is distributed among the heirs of the deceased.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on a dhimmi's built place of worship after his death. The author begins a new chapter on the will of a dhimmi, noting that non-Muslims follow Muslims in transactional matters. The specific ruling: If a Jew or Christian builds a synagogue or church during his health and then dies, the building becomes inheritance according to Abu Hanifa, who analogizes it to a waqf. In his view, a waqf is inheritable and not binding, so the same applies here. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) disagree: they consider the act of building a place of worship for a non-Muslim to be an act of disobedience (ma'siyah), and thus the building is not validly established as a religious endowment; consequently, it cannot be considered a waqf. The passage does not explicitly state which position is the mufta bihi, but the commentary explains that the building is distributed among heirs, reflecting the practical application of Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state, obligated to pay jizyah.
وقف (waqf): A charitable endowment; in Hanafi fiqh, according to Abu Hanifa, a waqf is not binding (ghayr lazim) and can be revoked by the founder.
معصیت (ma'siyah): An act of disobedience to Allah; here applied to building a place of worship for non-Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a synagogue built by a Jew during his health if he dies?
A) It becomes a waqf for the Jewish community and is not inheritable.
B) It becomes inheritance distributed among the heirs according to Abu Hanifa.
C) It is considered an invalid building and must be destroyed.
D) It automatically becomes a mosque for Muslims.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's built place of worship becomes inheritance under Abu Hanifa's analogy to waqf, while Sahibayn reject it as an act of disobedience; the practical consequence is whether the building is distributed among heirs or considered invalid.

Will of a Dhimmi to Build a Church for a Specified Group
Ruling on a dhimmi's bequest for a specific community

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a dhimmi's bequest to build a place of worship for a named community and explain the dual legal basis (istikhlaaf and tamleek) that validates it.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's bequest for a specified community's church is valid from one-third based on istikhlaaf and tamleek.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi wasiyya law: a non-Muslim subject (dhimmi) makes a bequest to convert his house into a church or synagogue for a designated group. The passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir, commented upon in Ashraf al-Hidaya, provides a clear ruling with a sophisticated legal rationale. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the dual nature of a bequest in Hanafi law—both as an appointment of a successor (istikhlaaf) and a transfer of ownership (tamleek).

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
The testator is a dhimmi (Jew or Christian). He bequeaths his house to be built as a church or synagogue for a specifically named community (e.g., 'the Melkites' or 'the Nestorians').
The bequest is for a building to be used as a place of worship, not for a vague purpose.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The bequest is valid (jāʾiz) and is executed from within one-third of the testator's estate. This is unanimous between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The one-third limit is the standard restriction for bequests to non-heirs in Islamic law.
3
Analyze the legal basis: dual nature of wasiyya
A bequest (wasiyya) in Hanafi law contains two potential legal meanings: (1) istikhlaaf – appointing someone as a manager or successor, and (2) tamleek – transferring ownership. A dhimmi has legal capacity (wilayah) for both. Under istikhlaaf, the bequest is valid as an appointment of the community to manage the property after death, limited to one-third. Under tamleek, the property becomes owned by the specified community, who can then do as they wish with it.
This dual analysis provides two independent grounds for validity, making the ruling robust.
4
Note the condition: specification of the community
The ruling applies only when the bequest is for a named, specific group (قوم مسمين). If the bequest is for a general, undefined group (e.g., 'all Christians'), the ruling may differ and a dispute exists among the Hanafi imams.
Specification ensures the beneficiary is identifiable and the bequest is not ambiguous.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi consensus
There is no disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) on this ruling. It is a established position from Zahir al-Riwayah, making it the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
Consensus within the school gives this ruling high authority in Hanafi fatwa.

یہودی یا نصرانی نے کسی معین قوم کیلئے اپنے گھر کو بیعہ یا کنیسہ بنانے کی وصیت کی ایسی وصیت کا حکم
قال و لو اوصی بذالک لقوم مسمين فهو من الثلث معناه اذا اوصى ان تبنى داره بيعة او كنيسة فهو جائز من الثلث لان الوصية فيها معنى الاستخلاف و معنى التمليك و له ولاية ذالک فامکن تصحیحه علی اعتبار المعنيين
ترجمہ امام آئمہ نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور اگر اس نے (یہودی یا نصرانی نے ) اس کی (بیعہ یا کنیسہ بنانے کی ) کسی معین قوم کیلئے وصیت کی پس وہ ثلث سے معتبر ہوگی اس کے معنی ہیں جبکہ وہ یہ وصیت کرے کہ اس کے گھر کو بیعہ یا کنیسہ بنادیا جائے تو یہ جائز ہے ایک تہائی سے اسلئے کہ وصیت میں استخلاف اور تملیک کے معنی ہیں اور ذمی کو اس کی (استخلاف اور تملیک کی ) ولایت ہے تو دونوں معنی کے اعتبار سے اس کی تصحیح ممکن ہے۔
تشریح پہلا مسئلہ تو میراث سے متعلق نہیں تھا اور یہ وصیت سے متعلق ہے فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر یہودی یا نصرانی نے یہ وصیت کی کہ میرے گھر کو بیعہ یا کنیسہ بنا دیا جائے تو یہ وصیت جائز ہے اور ثلث کے اندر نافذ ہوگی اور یہ حکم بالا اتفاق ہے جس میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف نہیں ہے مگر یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ وہ کسی معین مخصوص قوم کیلئے بیعہ یا کنیسہ بنانے کی وصیت کرے۔ کیونکہ یہ وصیت ہے اور وصیت کے اندر دو معنی پائے جاتے ہیں۔ 1- استخلاف 2- تملیک اور ذمی کیلئے اتنا بھی جائز ہے اور اس میں بھی جائز ہے تو خواہ اول معنی کا اعتبار کیا جائے تب بھی یہ وصیت جائز ہوگی اور خواہ دوسرے معنی تملیک کا لحاظ کیا جائے تب بھی یہ وصیت جائز ہوگی۔ تو استخلاف کی رعایت سے ہم نے ثلث تک اس کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اور تملیک کے معنی کی رعایت سے ہم نے کہا کہ اب یہ اس معین قوم کی ملکیت ہے وہ جو اس کا چاہیں کر سکتے ہیں۔
A Jew or a Christian made a will to make his house a church or synagogue for a specified community. The ruling on such a will: He (the imam) said: 'And if he makes a bequest for that (to build a church or synagogue) for a named group, then it is from the third.' Meaning: when he bequeaths that his house be built as a church or synagogue, it is permissible from the third because the bequest contains the meaning of succession (istikhlaaf) and the meaning of ownership transfer (tamleek). And he (the dhimmi) has authority over that, so it is possible to validate it by considering both meanings. Translation: The leading imams stated in al-Jami' al-Sagheer: 'And if he (the Jew or Christian) makes a bequest for that (building a church or synagogue) for a specified community, then it is valid from the third.' The meaning is that when he makes a bequest that his house be built as a church or synagogue, it is permissible from one-third of his estate because the bequest contains the meanings of istikhlaaf and tamleek, and the dhimmi has authority over that (istikhlaaf and tamleek), so it is possible to validate it by considering both meanings. Explanation: The first issue was related to inheritance, and this is related to bequest. He says: If a Jew or Christian makes a bequest to build a church or synagogue from his house, this bequest is valid and shall be executed from one-third of his estate. This ruling is unanimous between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn); there is no difference. However, this ruling applies when he makes the bequest for a specific, limited community. Because this is a bequest, and a bequest contains two meanings: 1) istikhlaaf (succession) and 2) tamleek (ownership transfer). And a dhimmi has authority in both matters; whether the first meaning is considered or the second, the bequest is valid. With regard to istikhlaaf, we deem it permissible up to one-third; with regard to tamleek, we say that the house becomes the property of that specific community, and they can do as they wish.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a bequest made by a non-Muslim subject (dhimmi) to build a church or synagogue from his own house for a named group. The immediate ruling: the bequest is valid and executed from within one-third of the testator's estate. The commentator (the author of Ashraf al-Hidaya) first quotes the Arabic text from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (a foundational text of Zahir al-Riwayah), then translates it, and finally provides an explanatory note (tashreeh). The ruling is unanimous across Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The reasoning given: a bequest inherently contains two aspects—istikhlaaf (appointing a successor in management) and tamleek (transferring ownership). Since the dhimmi has the legal capacity (wilaya) for both, the bequest can be validated on either basis. If viewed as istikhlaaf, the bequest is limited to one-third (the standard limit for bequests to non-heirs in Islamic law). If viewed as tamleek, the property transfers to the specified community, and they can dispose of it freely. This passage clarifies that the unanimous ruling only applies when the beneficiary is a specific, defined group; otherwise, as the next lesson shows, there is a dispute.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyya): A bequest or will made by a person, valid for up to one-third of the estate for non-heirs.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state.
استخلاف (istikhlaaf): Appointing someone as a successor or manager; here it means that the bequest can be seen as an appointment of the community to manage the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a dhimmi bequeaths his house to be built as a church for a specific named community, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) It is invalid because building a church is a sin.
B) It is valid only from one-third of the estate and is unanimous.
C) It is valid from the entire estate without restriction.
D) It is valid only if the dhimmi has no Muslim heirs.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's bequest to build a church or synagogue for a specified community is valid from one-third of the estate, based on the dual legal nature of wasiyya: succession and ownership transfer.
