Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Bequest for Unspecified Group: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest for unspecified community

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on a dhimmi's bequest for an unspecified community and apply the principle of considering the dhimmi's belief to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's bequest is judged by their belief, not Islamic objectivity.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding a dhimmi's bequest to build a synagogue or church for a general, unspecified community. The core question is whether the Islamic legal classification of the act (as sin or devotion) or the dhimmi's own religious classification determines validity. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to handle cases where the testator's belief system differs from Islamic norms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Scenario
A dhimmi bequeaths his house to be used as a synagogue for an unspecified community (ghayr mu'ayyan wa ghayr muhassar). Note that this is different from a bequest for a specific group, which was unanimously valid in the previous lesson.
The 'unspecified' condition triggers the dispute.
2
State the Sahibayn's Position and Proof
The Sahibayn rule the bequest invalid because building a place of worship for false religion is a sin (ma'siya) objectively in Islamic law. A bequest for a sin is invalid because executing it perpetuates sin.
They focus on the inherent nature of the act.
3
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Proof
Abu Hanifa rules the bequest valid because the dhimmi considers it an act of devotion (qurba). Muslims are commanded to leave dhimmis to their beliefs (Qur'an 109:6, etc.). He uses analogy: if a dhimmi bequeaths for a mosque (a sin in their belief), we invalidate it out of respect for their belief; similarly, we should validate based on their belief here.
He prioritizes subjective intent over objective classification.
4
Trace the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: For an unspecified community, Abu Hanifa's view allows execution of the will; the Sahibayn's view blocks it. Both agree if the community is specified.
Knowing this helps a mufti choose the operative view in context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مذکورہ وصیت غیر معین اور غیر محصور قوم کیلئے کرے تو کیا حکم ہے
قال و ان اوصى بداره کنیسة لقوم غير مسمين جازت الوصية عند ابي حنيفة وقالا الوصية باطلة لان هذه معصية حقيقة وان كان في معتقدهم قربة والوصية بالمعصية باطلة لما فى تنفيذها من تقرير المعصية
ترجمہ امام حمہ نے فرمایا اور اگر اس نے اپنا گھر کنیسہ بنانے کی وصیت کی غیر محصور قوم کیلئے تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وصیت جائز ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ وصیت باطل ہے اسلئے کہ یہ حقیقتا معصیت ہے اگر چہ ان کے اعتقاد میں قربت ہے اور معصیت کی وصیت باطل ہے اس وجہ سے کہ اس کے نافذ کرنے میں معصیت کو برقرار رکھنا ہے۔
تشریح اگر ذمی نے مذکورہ وصیت غیر معین اور غیر محصور قوم کے لئے کی تو اس میں اختلاف ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اب بھی وصیت جائز ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک باطل ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ وصیت فی نفسہ باطل ہے اگر چہ ذمیوں کے اعتقاد میں قربت ہے اور معصیت کی وصیت باطل ہے اس لئے کہ اگر اس کو نافذ کیا جائے گا تو معصیت اور باطل کو ہوا ملے گی۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل ولا بى حنيفة ان هذه قربة في معتقدهم و نحن امرنا بان نتركهم وما يدينون فتجوز بناء على اعتقادهم الايرى انه لو اوصى بما هو قربة حقيقة معصية فى معتقدهم لا تجوز الوصية اعتباراً لاعتقادهم فكذا عكسه ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ ان کے اعتقاد میں قربت ہے اور ہم کو حکم دیئے گئے ہیں کہ ان کو ان کے اعتقاد پر چھوڑ دیں تو یہ وصیت ان کے اعتقاد پر بنا کرتے ہوئے جائز ہے کیا یہ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر ذمی نے اس چیز کی وصیت کی جو حقیقہ قربت ہے ان کے اعتقاد میں معصیت ہے تو ان کے اعتقاد کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے وصیت جائز نہیں ہے تو ایسے ہی اس کا عکس ہوگا۔ تشریح یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ان کی وصایا کے جواز اور عدم جواز کا مدار ان کے اعتقاد کے مطابق قربت ہونے اور نہ ہونے پر ہے شریعت نے ہم کو حکم دیا ہے کہ ہم ذمیوں کے معتقدات سے تعرض نہ کریں اور ان کو ان کے اعتقاد پر چھوڑ دیں۔ اور یہاں ان کے اعتقاد میں یہ قربت ہے لہذا ہم نے اس کو صحیح کہہ دیا اور مسجد بنانے کی وصیت ان کے اعتقاد میں معصیت ہے تو ہم نے ان کے اعتقاد پر مدار رکھتے ہوئے اس کو باطل قرار دیدیا ہے۔
If he made the aforementioned bequest for an unspecified and unlimited community, what is the ruling? He said: 'And if he bequeaths his house as a synagogue for an unnamed group, the bequest is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said the bequest is invalid because this is truly a sin, even if in their belief it is an act of devotion. And a bequest for a sin is invalid because implementing it would establish the sin.' Translation: The imams said: And if he bequeaths his house to be built as a synagogue for an unspecified group, then according to Abu Hanifa the bequest is valid, while the Sahibayn said the bequest is invalid because it is truly a sin even if in their belief it is an act of devotion, and a bequest for a sin is invalid because implementing it would perpetuate the sin. Explanation: If a dhimmi makes the aforementioned bequest for an unspecified, unlimited group, there is a difference of opinion. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the bequest is still valid; according to the Sahibayn, it is invalid. The Sahibayn's evidence: this bequest is inherently invalid even if dhimmis believe it is devotional, and a bequest for a sin is invalid because if it is executed, it will give way to sin and falsehood. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence: 'And Abu Hanifa's argument: this is an act of devotion in their belief, and we have been commanded to leave them and their religion. So the bequest is valid based on their belief. Do you not see that if he bequeaths something that is truly an act of devotion but a sin in their belief, the bequest would not be valid, taking into account their belief? So similarly, the opposite applies.' Translation: And Abu Hanifa's evidence is that this is an act of devotion in their belief, and we have been commanded to leave them to their beliefs. So this bequest is valid based on their belief. Don't you see that if a dhimmi bequeaths something that is truly an act of devotion but is a sin in their belief, the bequest would not be valid, taking into account their belief? So likewise the reverse (applies). Explanation: This is Abu Hanifa's evidence, the gist of which is that the validity of their bequests depends on whether it is considered an act of devotion according to their belief. The Shariah has commanded us not to interfere with the beliefs of dhimmis and to leave them to their beliefs. Here, in their belief, this is devotion, so we deem it valid. And a bequest to build a mosque is a sin in their belief, so we declared it invalid based on their belief.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding a dhimmi's bequest to build a church or synagogue for a general, unspecified community. The Sahibayn argue that the act is inherently a sin (ma'siya) in Islamic law, even if the dhimmi considers it an act of worship. Since bequeathing for a sin is invalid, the bequest is void. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, bases the ruling on the dhimmi's own belief: because in their religion building a place of worship is a good deed (qurba), and Muslims are commanded not to interfere with their religious practices, the bequest is valid. He supports his view by analogy: if a dhimmi bequeaths something that is truly an act of worship in Islam (like building a mosque) but is a sin in their belief, we would consider their belief and invalidate the bequest. By the same logic, we should consider their belief here. The commentator (Ashraf al-Hidaya) provides the evidence and explanation for both sides. Note: This dispute only applies when the bequest is for an unspecified group (ghayr muhassar); for a specified group, the ruling was unanimous as seen in the previous lesson.

Key Terms
معصیت (ma'siya): A sin or act of disobedience to Allah. In this context, building a church is considered a sin in Islamic law, but the dhimmi considers it worship.
قربت (qurba): An act that brings one closer to God; an act of devotion. Here, the dhimmi's building of a place of worship is qurba in their belief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is a dhimmi's bequest to build a church for an unspecified community valid?
A) Because building a church is not a sin in Islamic law.
B) Because the bequest is limited to one-third of the estate.
C) Because the dhimmi considers it an act of devotion, and we leave them to their beliefs.
D) Because the Sahibayn's view is weak.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a dhimmi's bequest hinges on whether the act is qurba in their belief, not on Islamic objectivity, but only according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn uphold objective sin as the criterion.
